
Frankenstein
弗兰肯斯坦

By Mary Wollstonecraft Shelley
玛丽·沃斯通克拉夫特·雪莱

Letter 1
信1

To Mrs. Saville, England
致英国萨维尔夫人

St. Petersburgh, Dec. 11th, 17—
圣彼得堡，2017 年 12 月 11 日——

You will rejoice to hear that no disaster has accompanied the commencement of an enterprise which you have regarded with such evil forebodings. I arrived here yesterday, and my first task is to assure my dear sister of my welfare and increasing confidence in the success of my undertaking.
你会很高兴听到你怀有如此不祥预感的一项事业的开始并没有发生任何灾难。我昨天到达这里，我的首要任务是向我亲爱的妹妹保证我的幸福，并增强我事业成功的信心。

I am already far north of London, and as I walk in the streets of Petersburgh, I feel a cold northern breeze play upon my cheeks, which braces my nerves and fills me with delight. Do you understand this feeling? This breeze, which has travelled from the regions towards which I am advancing, gives me a foretaste of those icy climes. Inspirited by this wind of promise, my daydreams become more fervent and vivid. I try in vain to be persuaded that the pole is the seat of frost and desolation; it ever presents itself to my imagination as the region of beauty and delight. There, Margaret, the sun is forever visible, its broad disk just skirting the horizon and diffusing a perpetual splendour. There—for with your leave, my sister, I will put some trust in preceding navigators— there snow and frost are banished; and, sailing over a calm sea, we may be wafted to a land surpassing in wonders and in beauty every region hitherto discovered on the habitable globe. Its productions and features may be without example, as the phenomena of the heavenly bodies undoubtedly are in those undiscovered solitudes. What may not be expected in a country of eternal light? I may there discover the wondrous power which attracts the needle and may regulate a thousand celestial observations that require only this voyage to render their seeming eccentricities consistent forever. I shall satiate my ardent curiosity with the sight of a part of the world never before visited, and may tread a land never before imprinted by the foot of man. These are my enticements, and they are sufficient to conquer all fear of danger or death and to induce me to commence this labourious voyage with the joy a child feels when he embarks in a little boat, with his holiday mates, on an expedition of discovery up his native river. But supposing all these conjectures to be false, you cannot contest the inestimable benefit which I shall confer on all mankind, to the last generation, by discovering a passage near the pole to those countries, to reach which at present so many months are requisite; or by ascertaining the secret of the magnet, which, if at all possible, can only be effected by an undertaking such as mine.
我已远在伦敦以北，走在彼得堡的大街上，一股凛冽的北风拂过脸颊，使我的神经绷紧，心里充满愉悦。你明白这种感觉吗？这股微风从我即将前往的地区吹来，让我预尝到了那些冰冷的气候。在这承诺之风的鼓舞下，我的白日梦变得更加热烈和生动。我徒劳地试图说服杆子是霜冻和荒凉的所在地；它总是在我的想象中呈现出美丽和欢乐的境界。玛格丽特，在那里，太阳永远可见，它宽阔的圆盘正好位于地平线的边缘，散发出永恒的光彩。在那里——因为有了你的离开，我的姐妹，我会对前面的航海家抱有一些信任——那里的雪和霜都被消除了；当我们航行在平静的大海上时，我们可能会被漂流到一片神奇而美丽的土地，超越了迄今为止在可居住的地球上发现的每一个地区。它的产物和特征可能是无与伦比的，就像天体现象无疑存在于那些未被发现的孤独之中一样。在一个永恒之光的国家里，有什么是不可期待的呢？我可能会在那里发现吸引指针的奇妙力量，并可能调节一千个天体观测，而这些观测只需要这次航行就可以使它们看似怪异的现象永远一致。我将用看到世界上从未去过的地方的景象来满足我强烈的好奇心，并可能踏上人类从未留下过足迹的土地。 这些就是我的诱惑，它们足以克服对危险或死亡的所有恐惧，并诱使我带着孩子和他的度假伙伴登上小船进行发现探险时所感受到的快乐开始这次艰苦的航行。沿着他家乡的河流而上。但是，假设所有这些猜想都是错误的，你就无法质疑我将给全人类、直到最后一代人带来的不可估量的利益，因为我发现了一条靠近极地的通道，通往那些国家，目前需要几个月的时间才能到达这些国家。或者通过查明磁铁的秘密，如果可能的话，只能通过像我这样的事业来实现。

These reflections have dispelled the agitation with which I began my letter, and I feel my heart glow with an enthusiasm which elevates me to heaven, for nothing contributes so much to tranquillize the mind as a steady purpose—a point on which the soul may fix its intellectual eye. This expedition has been the favourite dream of my early years. I have read with ardour the accounts of the various voyages which have been made in the prospect of arriving at the North Pacific Ocean through the seas which surround the pole. You may remember that a history of all the voyages made for purposes of discovery composed the whole of our good Uncle Thomas’ library. My education was neglected, yet I was passionately fond of reading. These volumes were my study day and night, and my familiarity with them increased that regret which I had felt, as a child, on learning that my father’s dying injunction had forbidden my uncle to allow me to embark in a seafaring life.
这些思考驱散了我开始写这封信时的焦躁不安，我感到我的心洋溢着一种热情，这种热情使我升入天堂，因为没有什么比一个稳定的目标更能让心灵平静——一个灵魂可以固定的点。它的智慧之眼。这次探险是我早年最喜欢的梦想。我满怀热情地阅读了各种航行的记述，这些航行的目的是穿过极地周围的海洋到达北太平洋。您可能还记得，所有以发现为目的的航行的历史构成了我们善良的托马斯叔叔的整个图书馆。我的教育被忽视了，但我却非常喜欢读书。这些书是我夜以继日的学习，我对它们的熟悉增加了我小时候的遗憾，当我得知父亲的临终禁令禁止我的叔叔允许我开始航海生活时，我感到遗憾。

These visions faded when I perused, for the first time, those poets whose effusions entranced my soul and lifted it to heaven. I also became a poet and for one year lived in a paradise of my own creation; I imagined that I also might obtain a niche in the temple where the names of Homer and Shakespeare are consecrated. You are well acquainted with my failure and how heavily I bore the disappointment. But just at that time I inherited the fortune of my cousin, and my thoughts were turned into the channel of their earlier bent.
当我第一次细读那些诗人的诗篇时，这些幻象就消失了，他们的情感使我的灵魂着迷，并将其提升到天堂。我还成为了一名诗人，在我自己创造的天堂里生活了一年；我想象着我也可能在供奉荷马和莎士比亚名字的寺庙里获得一个壁龛。你很清楚我的失败以及我承受的失望有多大。但就在那时，我继承了表弟的财产，我的思想也转向了他们先前的倾向。

Six years have passed since I resolved on my present undertaking. I can, even now, remember the hour from which I dedicated myself to this great enterprise. I commenced by inuring my body to hardship. I accompanied the whale-fishers on several expeditions to the North Sea; I voluntarily endured cold, famine, thirst, and want of sleep; I often worked harder than the common sailors during the day and devoted my nights to the study of mathematics, the theory of medicine, and those branches of physical science from which a naval adventurer might derive the greatest practical advantage. Twice I actually hired myself as an under-mate in a Greenland whaler, and acquitted myself to admiration. I must own I felt a little proud when my captain offered me the second dignity in the vessel and entreated me to remain with the greatest earnestness, so valuable did he consider my services.
自从我决心从事目前的事业以来，已经过去了六年。即使现在，我仍然记得我为这个伟大事业奉献自己的时刻。我首先让自己的身体适应困难。我曾多次陪同捕鲸者前往北海探险。我自愿忍受寒冷、饥荒、口渴、失眠；我白天常常比普通水手更努力地工作，晚上则致力于研究数学、医学理论以及那些海军冒险家可能从中获得最大实际优势的物理科学分支。有两次，我实际上雇用了自己作为格陵兰捕鲸船上的小副手，并让自己无罪得令人钦佩。我必须承认，当我的船长向我提供船上的第二个尊严并恳求我以最大的诚意留下来时，我感到有点自豪，他认为我的服务非常有价值。

And now, dear Margaret, do I not deserve to accomplish some great purpose? My life might have been passed in ease and luxury, but I preferred glory to every enticement that wealth placed in my path. Oh, that some encouraging voice would answer in the affirmative! My courage and my resolution is firm; but my hopes fluctuate, and my spirits are often depressed. I am about to proceed on a long and difficult voyage, the emergencies of which will demand all my fortitude: I am required not only to raise the spirits of others, but sometimes to sustain my own, when theirs are failing.
现在，亲爱的玛格丽特，我难道不应该实现一些伟大的目标吗？我的一生也许过得安逸奢华，但我更喜欢荣耀，而不是财富给我带来的一切诱惑。哦，但愿有一些鼓励的声音会给出肯定的回答！我的勇气和决心是坚定的；但我的希望时常波动，精神时常消沉。我即将开始一次漫长而艰难的航行，其中的紧急情况将需要我全部的毅力：我不仅需要鼓舞他人的精神，有时还需要在他们的精神崩溃时支撑自己的精神。

This is the most favourable period for travelling in Russia. They fly quickly over the snow in their sledges; the motion is pleasant, and, in my opinion, far more agreeable than that of an English stagecoach. The cold is not excessive, if you are wrapped in furs— a dress which I have already adopted, for there is a great difference between walking the deck and remaining seated motionless for hours, when no exercise prevents the blood from actually freezing in your veins. I have no ambition to lose my life on the post-road between St. Petersburgh and Archangel.
这是俄罗斯旅游的最佳时期。他们驾着雪橇在雪地上飞快地飞翔。这个动作很令人愉快，而且在我看来，比英国驿马车的动作更令人愉快。如果你裹着毛皮——我已经穿上了这条裙子，那么寒冷并不算太冷，因为在甲板上行走和一动不动地坐着几个小时之间有很大的区别，因为没有任何运动可以阻止血液在静脉中真正冻结。 。我不想在圣彼得堡和阿尔汉格尔斯克之间的邮政公路上失去生命。

I shall depart for the latter town in a fortnight or three weeks; and my intention is to hire a ship there, which can easily be done by paying the insurance for the owner, and to engage as many sailors as I think necessary among those who are accustomed to the whale-fishing. I do not intend to sail until the month of June; and when shall I return? Ah, dear sister, how can I answer this question? If I succeed, many, many months, perhaps years, will pass before you and I may meet. If I fail, you will see me again soon, or never.
我将在两周或三周内前往后一个城镇。我的目的是在那里租一艘船，这可以很容易地通过为船主支付保险来完成，并在那些习惯于捕鲸的人中雇用我认为必要的尽可能多的水手。我不打算在六月之前启航；我什么时候回来？啊，亲爱的姐姐，这个问题我该怎么回答呢？如果我成功了，在你和我见面之前会过去很多很多个月，也许几年。如果我失败了，你很快就会再见到我，或者再也见不到我了。

Farewell, my dear, excellent Margaret. Heaven shower down blessings on you, and save me, that I may again and again testify my gratitude for all your love and kindness.
别了，我亲爱的、优秀的玛格丽特。上天赐福给你，拯救我，让我一次又一次地向你表达我对你的爱和善意的感激之情。

Your affectionate brother,
你深情的兄弟，

R. Walton
R·沃尔顿

Letter 2
信2

To Mrs. Saville, England
致英国萨维尔夫人

Archangel, 28th March, 17—
大天使，2017 年 3 月 28 日——

How slowly the time passes here, encompassed as I am by frost and snow! Yet a second step is taken towards my enterprise. I have hired a vessel and am occupied in collecting my sailors; those whom I have already engaged appear to be men on whom I can depend and are certainly possessed of dauntless courage.
在这里，时间过得多么缓慢，就像我被霜雪包围一样！然而，我的事业又迈出了第二步。我租了一艘船，正忙于召集我的水手；我已经聘用的那些人看来是我可以依靠的人，而且肯定拥有大无畏的勇气。

But I have one want which I have never yet been able to satisfy, and the absence of the object of which I now feel as a most severe evil. I have no friend, Margaret: when I am glowing with the enthusiasm of success, there will be none to participate my joy; if I am assailed by disappointment, no one will endeavour to sustain me in dejection. I shall commit my thoughts to paper, it is true; but that is a poor medium for the communication of feeling. I desire the company of a man who could sympathize with me, whose eyes would reply to mine. You may deem me romantic, my dear sister, but I bitterly feel the want of a friend. I have no one near me, gentle yet courageous, possessed of a cultivated as well as of a capacious mind, whose tastes are like my own, to approve or amend my plans. How would such a friend repair the faults of your poor brother! I am too ardent in execution and too impatient of difficulties. But it is a still greater evil to me that I am self-educated: for the first fourteen years of my life I ran wild on a common and read nothing but our Uncle Thomas’ books of voyages. At that age I became acquainted with the celebrated poets of our own country; but it was only when it had ceased to be in my power to derive its most important benefits from such a conviction that I perceived the necessity of becoming acquainted with more languages than that of my native country. Now I am twenty-eight and am in reality more illiterate than many schoolboys of fifteen. It is true that I have thought more and that my daydreams are more extended and magnificent, but they want (as the painters call it) *keeping*; and I greatly need a friend who would have sense enough not to despise me as romantic, and affection enough for me to endeavour to regulate my mind.
但我有一个我从未能够满足的愿望，而我现在觉得缺乏这个对象是一种最严重的罪恶。我没有朋友，玛格丽特：当我洋溢着成功的热情时，没有人能分享我的喜悦；如果我感到失望，没有人会尽力让我保持沮丧。我将把我的想法写在纸上，这是真的；但这对于交流感情来说是一个很糟糕的媒介。我渴望有一个能同情我、能用眼神回应我的人为伴。你可能认为我很浪漫，我亲爱的妹妹，但我痛苦地感到需要一个朋友。我身边没有一个温和而勇敢、有教养且思想宽广、品味与我相似的人来批准或修改我的计划。这样的朋友怎么能弥补你可怜兄弟的过错呢！我执行力太热心，遇到困难太不耐烦。但对我来说，更大的祸害是我自学成才：在我生命的头十四年里，我在公共场所疯狂地生活，除了托马斯叔叔的航海书籍外，我什么也不读。在那个年纪，我结识了我国的著名诗人。但只有当我不再能够从这样的信念中获得最重要的利益时，我才意识到有必要熟悉比我的祖国更多的语言。现在我二十八岁了，实际上我比许多十五岁的男学生还要文盲。确实，我想得更多，我的白日梦更广阔、更宏伟，但它们想要（正如画家所说的）“保留”；我非常需要一个有足够理智的朋友，不会因为我浪漫而鄙视我，也有足够的感情，让我努力调节自己的思想。

Well, these are useless complaints; I shall certainly find no friend on the wide ocean, nor even here in Archangel, among merchants and seamen. Yet some feelings, unallied to the dross of human nature, beat even in these rugged bosoms. My lieutenant, for instance, is a man of wonderful courage and enterprise; he is madly desirous of glory, or rather, to word my phrase more characteristically, of advancement in his profession. He is an Englishman, and in the midst of national and professional prejudices, unsoftened by cultivation, retains some of the noblest endowments of humanity. I first became acquainted with him on board a whale vessel; finding that he was unemployed in this city, I easily engaged him to assist in my enterprise.
好吧，这些都是无用的抱怨；我肯定不会在广阔的海洋上找到朋友，甚至在天使长这里的商人和海员中也找不到朋友。然而，有些情感，与人性的渣滓无关，甚至在这些崎岖的胸怀中也跳动着。例如，我的中尉是一个非常有勇气和进取心的人。他疯狂地渴望荣耀，或者更确切地说，用我更典型的说法，渴望在他的职业中取得进步。他是一个英国人，在民族和职业偏见中，没有因教养而软化，保留了一些人类最崇高的天赋。我第一次认识他是在一艘捕鲸船上。发现他在这个城市失业了，我就轻易聘请他来协助我的企业。

The master is a person of an excellent disposition and is remarkable in the ship for his gentleness and the mildness of his discipline. This circumstance, added to his well-known integrity and dauntless courage, made me very desirous to engage him. A youth passed in solitude, my best years spent under your gentle and feminine fosterage, has so refined the groundwork of my character that I cannot overcome an intense distaste to the usual brutality exercised on board ship: I have never believed it to be necessary, and when I heard of a mariner equally noted for his kindliness of heart and the respect and obedience paid to him by his crew, I felt myself peculiarly fortunate in being able to secure his services. I heard of him first in rather a romantic manner, from a lady who owes to him the happiness of her life. This, briefly, is his story. Some years ago he loved a young Russian lady of moderate fortune, and having amassed a considerable sum in prize-money, the father of the girl consented to the match. He saw his mistress once before the destined ceremony; but she was bathed in tears, and throwing herself at his feet, entreated him to spare her, confessing at the same time that she loved another, but that he was poor, and that her father would never consent to the union. My generous friend reassured the suppliant, and on being informed of the name of her lover, instantly abandoned his pursuit. He had already bought a farm with his money, on which he had designed to pass the remainder of his life; but he bestowed the whole on his rival, together with the remains of his prize-money to purchase stock, and then himself solicited the young woman’s father to consent to her marriage with her lover. But the old man decidedly refused, thinking himself bound in honour to my friend, who, when he found the father inexorable, quitted his country, nor returned until he heard that his former mistress was married according to her inclinations. ‘What a noble fellow!’ you will exclaim. He is so; but then he is wholly uneducated: he is as silent as a Turk, and a kind of ignorant carelessness attends him, which, while it renders his conduct the more astonishing, detracts from the interest and sympathy which otherwise he would command.
船长是一位性情优秀的人，在船上以他的温和和温和的纪律而著称。这种情况，再加上他众所周知的正直和无畏的勇气，使我非常想与他交往。我的青春在孤独中度过，我最美好的时光是在您温柔而女性化的养育下度过的，这使我的性格基础如此完善，以至于我无法克服对船上常见的野蛮行径的强烈厌恶：我从来不认为有必要，当我听说一位水手同样以他的善良之心以及他的船员对他的尊重和服从而闻名时，我感到自己特别幸运，能够获得他的服务。我第一次以一种相当浪漫的方式从一位女士那里听说了他，她一生的幸福归功于他。简而言之，这就是他的故事。几年前，他爱上了一位富有的俄罗斯年轻女士，在积攒了一大笔奖金后，女孩的父亲同意了这门亲事。在预定的仪式之前，他见过他的情妇一次；但她泪流满面，扑倒在他的脚下，恳求他饶恕她，同时承认她爱着另一个人，但他很穷，而且她的父亲永远不会同意他们的结合。我慷慨的朋友安抚了恳求者，并在得知她爱人的名字后，立即放弃了他的追求。他已经用自己的钱买了一座农场，打算在里面度过余生。但他把全部财产连同剩余的奖金都捐给了他的对手，用于购买股票，然后他亲自恳求这位年轻女子的父亲同意她与她的情人结婚。 但老人断然拒绝，认为自己是为了尊重我的朋友，当他发现父亲无情时，他离开了自己的国家，直到听说他的前情妇按照她的意愿结婚了才回来。 “多么高尚的人啊！”你会惊叹道。他很;但他完全没有受过教育：他像土耳其人一样沉默，他身上有一种无知的粗心，这虽然使他的行为更加令人惊讶，但却减损了他本来可以得到的兴趣和同情。

Yet do not suppose, because I complain a little or because I can conceive a consolation for my toils which I may never know, that I am wavering in my resolutions. Those are as fixed as fate, and my voyage is only now delayed until the weather shall permit my embarkation. The winter has been dreadfully severe, but the spring promises well, and it is considered as a remarkably early season, so that perhaps I may sail sooner than I expected. I shall do nothing rashly: you know me sufficiently to confide in my prudence and considerateness whenever the safety of others is committed to my care.
然而，不要因为我有一点抱怨，或者因为我能为我的辛劳找到一个我可能永远不知道的安慰，就认为我的决心动摇了。这些就像命运一样注定，我的航程现在才被推迟，直到天气允许我上船。冬天严酷得可怕，但春天却充满希望，而且这被认为是一个非常早的季节，所以也许我可以比我预期的更早起航。我不会鲁莽行事：您足够了解我，相信每当我照顾他人的安全时，我都会谨慎而体贴。

I cannot describe to you my sensations on the near prospect of my undertaking. It is impossible to communicate to you a conception of the trembling sensation, half pleasurable and half fearful, with which I am preparing to depart. I am going to unexplored regions, to ‘the land of mist and snow,’ but I shall kill no albatross; therefore do not be alarmed for my safety or if I should come back to you as worn and woeful as the ‘Ancient Mariner.’ You will smile at my allusion, but I will disclose a secret. I have often attributed my attachment to, my passionate enthusiasm for, the dangerous mysteries of ocean to that production of the most imaginative of modern poets. There is something at work in my soul which I do not understand. I am practically industrious—painstaking, a workman to execute with perseverance and labour—but besides this there is a love for the marvellous, a belief in the marvellous, intertwined in all my projects, which hurries me out of the common pathways of men, even to the wild sea and unvisited regions I am about to explore.
我无法向你描述我对我的事业的近期前景的感受。我无法向你们传达我准备离开时那种半愉悦半恐惧的颤抖感觉。我要去未开发的地方，去“雾雪之地”，但我不会杀死信天翁；因此，请不要担心我的安全，也不要担心我会像“古代水手”一样疲惫而悲伤地回到你身边。你会对我的暗示微笑，但我会透露一个秘密。我经常将我对海洋危险奥秘的依恋和热情归因于最富有想象力的现代诗人的作品。我的灵魂里有某种我不明白的东西在起作用。我实际上很勤奋——吃苦耐劳，是一个以毅力和劳动来执行的工人——但除此之外，还有一种对奇妙事物的热爱，一种对奇妙事物的信仰，这些都交织在我所有的项目中，这促使我脱离了人类的共同道路，甚至到我即将探索的狂野大海和人迹罕至的地区。

But to return to dearer considerations. Shall I meet you again, after having traversed immense seas, and returned by the most southern cape of Africa or America? I dare not expect such success, yet I cannot bear to look on the reverse of the picture. Continue for the present to write to me by every opportunity: I may receive your letters on some occasions when I need them most to support my spirits. I love you very tenderly. Remember me with affection, should you never hear from me again.
但回到更重要的考虑。跨越大海，从非洲或美洲最南端的海角归来后，我还能再次见到你吗？我不敢奢望如此成功，但我又不忍心看照片的反面。继续利用一切机会给我写信：我可能会在某些场合收到你的来信，当我最需要它们来支撑我的精神时。我非常温柔地爱你。深情地记住我，如果你再也没有收到我的消息。

Your affectionate brother,
你深情的兄弟，

Robert Walton
罗伯特·沃尔顿

Letter 3
信3

To Mrs. Saville, England
致英国萨维尔夫人

July 7th, 17—
2017 年 7 月 7 日——

My dear Sister,
亲爱的姐姐，

I write a few lines in haste to say that I am safe— and well advanced on my voyage. This letter will reach England by a merchantman now on its homeward voyage from Archangel; more fortunate than I, who may not see my native land, perhaps, for many years. I am, however, in good spirits: my men are bold and apparently firm of purpose, nor do the floating sheets of ice that continually pass us, indicating the dangers of the region towards which we are advancing, appear to dismay them. We have already reached a very high latitude; but it is the height of summer, and although not so warm as in England, the southern gales, which blow us speedily towards those shores which I so ardently desire to attain, breathe a degree of renovating warmth which I had not expected.
我匆忙写下几行文字，表示我很安全，并且在航行中进展顺利。这封信将由一艘正在从大天使岛返航的商船到达英国；比我幸运，也许很多年都见不到我的祖国了。不过，我的精神状态很好：我的士兵们很勇敢，而且意志坚定，不断从我们身边经过的浮冰表明我们正在前进的地区存在危险，似乎也没有让他们感到沮丧。我们已经到达了一个很高的纬度；但现在正值盛夏，虽然不像英国那样温暖，但南方的大风将我们迅速吹向我热切渴望到达的海岸，带来了我意想不到的令人耳目一新的温暖。

No incidents have hitherto befallen us that would make a figure in a letter. One or two stiff gales and the springing of a leak are accidents which experienced navigators scarcely remember to record, and I shall be well content if nothing worse happen to us during our voyage.
迄今为止，我们还没有遇到过能在信中留下深刻印象的事件。一两次大风和突然出现的泄漏都是经验丰富的航海家几乎不记得记录的事故，如果我们在航行期间没有发生更糟糕的事情，我会很满意。

Adieu, my dear Margaret. Be assured that for my own sake, as well as yours, I will not rashly encounter danger. I will be cool, persevering, and prudent.
再见，我亲爱的玛格丽特。请放心，为了我自己，也为了你，我不会贸然遭遇危险。我会冷静、坚持、谨慎。

But success *shall* crown my endeavours. Wherefore not? Thus far I have gone, tracing a secure way over the pathless seas, the very stars themselves being witnesses and testimonies of my triumph. Why not still proceed over the untamed yet obedient element? What can stop the determined heart and resolved will of man?
但成功*将*为我的努力加冕。为什么不呢？到目前为止，我已经在无路的海洋上找到了一条安全的道路，连星星本身就是我胜利的见证和见证。为什么不继续处理未驯服但听话的元素呢？什么能阻挡人坚定的心和坚定的意志呢？

My swelling heart involuntarily pours itself out thus. But I must finish. Heaven bless my beloved sister!
我那颗膨胀的心不由自主地就这样流露出来了。但我必须完成。愿上天保佑我亲爱的妹妹！

R.W.

Letter 4
信4

To Mrs. Saville, England
致英国萨维尔夫人

August 5th, 17—
2017 年 8 月 5 日——

So strange an accident has happened to us that I cannot forbear recording it, although it is very probable that you will see me before these papers can come into your possession.
我们发生了一场如此奇怪的事故，以至于我忍不住把它记录下来，尽管你很有可能在这些文件到达你手中之前见到我。

Last Monday (July 31st) we were nearly surrounded by ice, which closed in the ship on all sides, scarcely leaving her the sea-room in which she floated. Our situation was somewhat dangerous, especially as we were compassed round by a very thick fog. We accordingly lay to, hoping that some change would take place in the atmosphere and weather.
上周一（7 月 31 日），我们几乎被冰包围了，船的四面八方都被冰封住了，几乎没有留下她漂浮的海室。我们的处境有些危险，尤其是当我们被浓雾包围时。我们因此而躺下，希望大气和天气会发生一些变化。

About two o’clock the mist cleared away, and we beheld, stretched out in every direction, vast and irregular plains of ice, which seemed to have no end. Some of my comrades groaned, and my own mind began to grow watchful with anxious thoughts, when a strange sight suddenly attracted our attention and diverted our solicitude from our own situation. We perceived a low carriage, fixed on a sledge and drawn by dogs, pass on towards the north, at the distance of half a mile; a being which had the shape of a man, but apparently of gigantic stature, sat in the sledge and guided the dogs. We watched the rapid progress of the traveller with our telescopes until he was lost among the distant inequalities of the ice.
大约两点钟左右，雾气散去，我们看到了向四面八方延伸的广阔而不规则的冰原，似乎没有尽头。一些战友发出了呻吟声，而我自己的心也开始变得警惕起来，充满了焦虑的想法，这时，一个奇怪的景象突然引起了我们的注意，转移了我们对自己处境的关心。我们看到一辆低矮的马车，固定在雪橇上，由狗拉着，向北行驶，距离半英里；一个人形的存在，但显然身材巨大，坐在雪橇上引导着狗。我们用望远镜观察着旅行者的快速行进，直到他消失在遥远的冰层中。

This appearance excited our unqualified wonder. We were, as we believed, many hundred miles from any land; but this apparition seemed to denote that it was not, in reality, so distant as we had supposed. Shut in, however, by ice, it was impossible to follow his track, which we had observed with the greatest attention.
这个出现让我们感到无比的惊奇。正如我们所相信的，我们距离任何陆地都有数百英里。但这个幽灵似乎表明，事实上，它并不像我们想象的那么遥远。然而，由于被冰封住，我们不可能追踪他的踪迹，而我们曾非常仔细地观察过他的踪迹。

About two hours after this occurrence we heard the ground sea, and before night the ice broke and freed our ship. We, however, lay to until the morning, fearing to encounter in the dark those large loose masses which float about after the breaking up of the ice. I profited of this time to rest for a few hours.
事件发生后大约两个小时，我们听到了地面海浪的声音，在入夜前，冰层破裂并释放了我们的船。然而，我们一直睡到早上，担心在黑暗中遇到那些冰块破裂后漂浮的大块松散的物体。我利用这段时间休息了几个小时。

In the morning, however, as soon as it was light, I went upon deck and found all the sailors busy on one side of the vessel, apparently talking to someone in the sea. It was, in fact, a sledge, like that we had seen before, which had drifted towards us in the night on a large fragment of ice. Only one dog remained alive; but there was a human being within it whom the sailors were persuading to enter the vessel. He was not, as the other traveller seemed to be, a savage inhabitant of some undiscovered island, but a European. When I appeared on deck the master said, ‘Here is our captain, and he will not allow you to perish on the open sea.’
然而，早上天一亮，我就走到甲板上，发现所有的水手都在船的一侧忙碌着，显然是在和海里的某个人说话。事实上，它是一个雪橇，就像我们以前见过的那样，它在夜间在一大块冰块上向我们漂来。只有一只狗还活着；但里面有一个人，水手们正在劝说他进入船内。他并不像另一位旅行者那样，是某个未被发现的岛屿上的野蛮居民，而是一个欧洲人。当我出现在甲板上时，船长说：“这是我们的船长，他不会允许你在公海上灭亡。”

On perceiving me, the stranger addressed me in English, although with a foreign accent. ‘Before I come on board your vessel,’ said he, ‘will you have the kindness to inform me whither you are bound?’
陌生人一看到我，就用英语跟我说话，尽管带有外国口音。 “在我登上你的船之前，”他说，“能否请你告诉我你要去哪里？”

You may conceive my astonishment on hearing such a question addressed to me from a man on the brink of destruction and to whom I should have supposed that my vessel would have been a resource which he would not have exchanged for the most precious wealth the earth can afford. I replied, however, that we were on a voyage of discovery towards the northern pole.
你可能会想象，当我听到一个濒临毁灭的人向我提出这样的问题时，我会感到多么惊讶，对他来说，我本应该认为我的船只是一种资源，他不会用地球上最宝贵的财富来交换。买得起。然而，我回答说，我们正在前往北极的发现之旅中。

Upon hearing this he appeared satisfied and consented to come on board. Good God! Margaret, if you had seen the man who thus capitulated for his safety, your surprise would have been boundless. His limbs were nearly frozen, and his body dreadfully emaciated by fatigue and suffering. I never saw a man in so wretched a condition. We attempted to carry him into the cabin, but as soon as he had quitted the fresh air he fainted. We accordingly brought him back to the deck and restored him to animation by rubbing him with brandy and forcing him to swallow a small quantity. As soon as he showed signs of life we wrapped him up in blankets and placed him near the chimney of the kitchen stove. By slow degrees he recovered and ate a little soup, which restored him wonderfully.
听了这话，他显得很满意，同意上船。天哪！玛格丽特，如果你看到那个为了自己的安全而投降的人，你一定会感到无比惊讶。他的四肢几乎冻僵了，身体因疲劳和痛苦而瘦得可怕。我从未见过一个人处于如此悲惨的境地。我们试图把他抱进机舱，但他一离开新鲜空气就晕倒了。因此，我们把他带回甲板上，用白兰地擦他并强迫他吞下少量，使他恢复活力。当他出现生命迹象时，我们就用毯子把他包裹起来，把他放在厨房炉灶的烟囱附近。他慢慢地康复了，喝了一点汤，恢复得非常好。

Two days passed in this manner before he was able to speak, and I often feared that his sufferings had deprived him of understanding. When he had in some measure recovered, I removed him to my own cabin and attended on him as much as my duty would permit. I never saw a more interesting creature: his eyes have generally an expression of wildness, and even madness, but there are moments when, if anyone performs an act of kindness towards him or does him the most trifling service, his whole countenance is lighted up, as it were, with a beam of benevolence and sweetness that I never saw equalled. But he is generally melancholy and despairing, and sometimes he gnashes his teeth, as if impatient of the weight of woes that oppresses him.
就这样过了两天，他才能够说话，我常常担心他的痛苦使他失去了理解力。当他在某种程度上康复后，我把他带到我自己的小屋，并在我的职责允许的范围内照顾他。我从来没有见过比他更有趣的生物：他的眼睛通常流露出狂野，甚至疯狂的表情，但有时，如果有人对他做出善意的举动，或者为他提供最微不足道的服务，他的整个脸都会发光。可以说，带着我从未见过的仁慈和甜蜜的光芒。但他总体上是忧郁和绝望的，有时他会咬牙切齿，似乎对压在他身上的不幸的重压感到不耐烦。

When my guest was a little recovered I had great trouble to keep off the men, who wished to ask him a thousand questions; but I would not allow him to be tormented by their idle curiosity, in a state of body and mind whose restoration evidently depended upon entire repose. Once, however, the lieutenant asked why he had come so far upon the ice in so strange a vehicle.
当我的客人稍稍恢复过来时，我费了好大劲才阻止那些想问他一千个问题的人。但我不允许他受到他们无谓的好奇心的折磨，因为他的身心状态显然取决于完全的休息。然而，有一次，中尉问他为什么乘坐如此奇怪的车辆在冰面上走了这么远。

His countenance instantly assumed an aspect of the deepest gloom, and he replied, ‘To seek one who fled from me.’
他的脸色顿时变得极为阴沉，回答道：“寻找一个从我身边逃走的人。”

‘And did the man whom you pursued travel in the same fashion?’
“你追寻的那个男人也以同样的方式旅行吗？”

‘Yes.’
'是的。'

‘Then I fancy we have seen him, for the day before we picked you up we saw some dogs drawing a sledge, with a man in it, across the ice.’
“那么我想我们见过他，因为在我们接你的前一天，我们看到一些狗在冰面上拉着一个雪橇，里面有一个人。”

This aroused the stranger’s attention, and he asked a multitude of questions concerning the route which the demon, as he called him, had pursued. Soon after, when he was alone with me, he said, ‘I have, doubtless, excited your curiosity, as well as that of these good people; but you are too considerate to make inquiries.’
这引起了陌生人的注意，他问了很多关于恶魔（他这样称呼他）所走的路线的问题。不久之后，当他单独和我在一起时，他说：“毫无疑问，我激发了你以及这些好人的好奇心；但你太体贴了，没有打听。”

‘Certainly; it would indeed be very impertinent and inhuman of me to trouble you with any inquisitiveness of mine.’
'当然;如果我以任何好奇心来打扰你，那确实是非常无礼和不人道的。

‘And yet you rescued me from a strange and perilous situation; you have benevolently restored me to life.’
‘然而你却把我从奇怪而危险的境地中救了出来；你仁慈地让我复活了。”

Soon after this he inquired if I thought that the breaking up of the ice had destroyed the other sledge. I replied that I could not answer with any degree of certainty, for the ice had not broken until near midnight, and the traveller might have arrived at a place of safety before that time; but of this I could not judge.
此后不久，他问我是否认为冰的破裂已经毁坏了另一个雪橇。我回答说，我无法给出任何确定的答案，因为冰直到接近午夜才破裂，旅行者可能在那之前就到达了安全地点；但对此我无法判断。

From this time a new spirit of life animated the decaying frame of the stranger. He manifested the greatest eagerness to be upon deck to watch for the sledge which had before appeared; but I have persuaded him to remain in the cabin, for he is far too weak to sustain the rawness of the atmosphere. I have promised that someone should watch for him and give him instant notice if any new object should appear in sight.
从那时起，一种新的生命精神使这个陌生人腐烂的身体焕发了生机。他表现出极大的渴望，想要到甲板上寻找先前出现的雪橇。但我说服他留在小屋里，因为他太虚弱了，无法承受恶劣的气氛。我已经答应有人会留意他，并在看到任何新物体时立即通知他。

Such is my journal of what relates to this strange occurrence up to the present day. The stranger has gradually improved in health but is very silent and appears uneasy when anyone except myself enters his cabin. Yet his manners are so conciliating and gentle that the sailors are all interested in him, although they have had very little communication with him. For my own part, I begin to love him as a brother, and his constant and deep grief fills me with sympathy and compassion. He must have been a noble creature in his better days, being even now in wreck so attractive and amiable.
这就是我迄今为止与这一奇怪事件有关的日记。陌生人的健康状况逐渐好转，但非常沉默，当除了我之外的任何人进入他的小屋时，他都会显得不安。然而他的举止是如此的和蔼可亲和温柔，以至于水手们都对他很感兴趣，尽管他们与他的交流很少。就我而言，我开始像兄弟一样爱他，他持续而深切的悲伤让我充满同情和怜悯。在他好的日子里，他一定是一位高贵的人，即使现在处于困境，他仍然如此迷人和和蔼可亲。

I said in one of my letters, my dear Margaret, that I should find no friend on the wide ocean; yet I have found a man who, before his spirit had been broken by misery, I should have been happy to have possessed as the brother of my heart.
亲爱的玛格丽特，我在一封信中说，在广阔的海洋上我找不到朋友；然而，我发现了一个人，在他的精神被苦难击垮之前，我会很高兴能拥有他作为我的心上兄弟。

I shall continue my journal concerning the stranger at intervals, should I have any fresh incidents to record.
如果我有任何新的事件需要记录，我将不时地继续写关于陌生人的日记。

August 13th, 17—
2017 年 8 月 13 日——

My affection for my guest increases every day. He excites at once my admiration and my pity to an astonishing degree. How can I see so noble a creature destroyed by misery without feeling the most poignant grief? He is so gentle, yet so wise; his mind is so cultivated, and when he speaks, although his words are culled with the choicest art, yet they flow with rapidity and unparalleled eloquence.
我对客人的感情与日俱增。他立刻激起了我的钦佩和怜悯，达到了惊人的程度。看到如此高贵的生物被苦难摧毁，我怎能不感到最心酸的悲伤呢？他是那么温柔，却又那么睿智；他的心性如此修养，说话的时候，虽然语言精雕细琢，但行云流水，雄辩无比。

He is now much recovered from his illness and is continually on the deck, apparently watching for the sledge that preceded his own. Yet, although unhappy, he is not so utterly occupied by his own misery but that he interests himself deeply in the projects of others. He has frequently conversed with me on mine, which I have communicated to him without disguise. He entered attentively into all my arguments in favour of my eventual success and into every minute detail of the measures I had taken to secure it. I was easily led by the sympathy which he evinced to use the language of my heart, to give utterance to the burning ardour of my soul, and to say, with all the fervour that warmed me, how gladly I would sacrifice my fortune, my existence, my every hope, to the furtherance of my enterprise. One man’s life or death were but a small price to pay for the acquirement of the knowledge which I sought, for the dominion I should acquire and transmit over the elemental foes of our race. As I spoke, a dark gloom spread over my listener’s countenance. At first I perceived that he tried to suppress his emotion; he placed his hands before his eyes, and my voice quivered and failed me as I beheld tears trickle fast from between his fingers; a groan burst from his heaving breast. I paused; at length he spoke, in broken accents: ‘Unhappy man! Do you share my madness? Have you drunk also of the intoxicating draught? Hear me; let me reveal my tale, and you will dash the cup from your lips!’
现在，他的病已经痊愈很多，并且一直在甲板上，显然是在寻找先于他自己的雪橇。然而，尽管他不快乐，但他并没有完全沉浸在自己的痛苦之中，而是对他人的计划深感兴趣。他经常与我谈论我的事情，我也毫不掩饰地传达给他。他仔细地了解了我所有支持我最终成功的论点，以及我为确保成功而采取的措施的每一个细节。我很容易被他所表现出的同情所引导，用我内心的语言，表达我灵魂中燃烧的热情，并以所有温暖我的热情说，我多么乐意牺牲我的财产，我的财产。存在，是我的每一个希望，是为了我的事业的发展。为了获得我所寻求的知识，为了获得并传递对我们种族的基本敌人的统治权，一个人的生或死只是一个小小的代价。当我说话时，听者的脸上浮现出一种阴沉的表情。起初我察觉到他试图压抑自己的情绪；但他并没有这么做。他把手放在眼前，当我看到泪水从他的手指间快速流下时，我的声音颤抖着，失语了。他起伏的胸膛里发出一声呻吟。我停了下来；最后他用断断续续的口音说道：“不幸的人！”你和我一样疯狂吗？你也喝过醉人的酒吗？听我说;让我揭露我的故事，你就会把杯子从嘴上摔下来！

Such words, you may imagine, strongly excited my curiosity; but the paroxysm of grief that had seized the stranger overcame his weakened powers, and many hours of repose and tranquil conversation were necessary to restore his composure.
你可以想象，这些话强烈地激发了我的好奇心。但这位陌生人突然爆发的悲痛克服了他虚弱的力量，需要许多小时的休息和平静的谈话才能恢复他的镇静。

Having conquered the violence of his feelings, he appeared to despise himself for being the slave of passion; and quelling the dark tyranny of despair, he led me again to converse concerning myself personally. He asked me the history of my earlier years. The tale was quickly told, but it awakened various trains of reflection. I spoke of my desire of finding a friend, of my thirst for a more intimate sympathy with a fellow mind than had ever fallen to my lot, and expressed my conviction that a man could boast of little happiness who did not enjoy this blessing.
在克服了强烈的感情之后，他似乎鄙视自己是激情的奴隶。他平息了绝望的黑暗暴政，让我再次谈论我自己。他问我早年的经历。这个故事很快就被讲述了，但它却引发了一系列的反思。我谈到了我想要找到一个朋友的愿望，我渴望与同胞有比我的命运更亲密的同情，并表达了我的信念，一个人如果不享受这种祝福，就不能夸耀什么幸福。

‘I agree with you,’ replied the stranger; ‘we are unfashioned creatures, but half made up, if one wiser, better, dearer than ourselves— such a friend ought to be—do not lend his aid to perfectionate our weak and faulty natures. I once had a friend, the most noble of human creatures, and am entitled, therefore, to judge respecting friendship. You have hope, and the world before you, and have no cause for despair. But I—I have lost everything and cannot begin life anew.’
“我同意你的看法，”陌生人回答道。 “我们是不合时宜的生物，但半成品，如果有一个比我们更聪明、更好、更可爱的人——这样的朋友就应该是——不要帮助我们完善我们软弱和有缺陷的本性。我曾经有一个朋友，他是人类中最崇高的朋友，因此有权判断是否尊重友谊。你有希望，世界就在你面前，没有理由绝望。但我——我失去了一切，无法重新开始生活。

As he said this his countenance became expressive of a calm, settled grief that touched me to the heart. But he was silent and presently retired to his cabin.
当他说这句话的时候，他的表情变得平静、安定的悲伤，让我的心感动不已。但他沉默了，不久就回到了自己的小屋。

Even broken in spirit as he is, no one can feel more deeply than he does the beauties of nature. The starry sky, the sea, and every sight afforded by these wonderful regions seem still to have the power of elevating his soul from earth. Such a man has a double existence: he may suffer misery and be overwhelmed by disappointments, yet when he has retired into himself, he will be like a celestial spirit that has a halo around him, within whose circle no grief or folly ventures.
即使他精神崩溃，也没有人能比他更深刻地感受到大自然的美丽。星空、大海，这些美妙的地方所呈现的每一处景色，似乎仍然有让他的灵魂升华的力量。这样的人具有双重存在：他可能遭受苦难，被失望压垮，但当他退隐到自己的世界时，他就像一个环绕着光环的天神，在它的圆圈内没有悲伤或愚蠢的冒险。

Will you smile at the enthusiasm I express concerning this divine wanderer? You would not if you saw him. You have been tutored and refined by books and retirement from the world, and you are therefore somewhat fastidious; but this only renders you the more fit to appreciate the extraordinary merits of this wonderful man. Sometimes I have endeavoured to discover what quality it is which he possesses that elevates him so immeasurably above any other person I ever knew. I believe it to be an intuitive discernment, a quick but never-failing power of judgment, a penetration into the causes of things, unequalled for clearness and precision; add to this a facility of expression and a voice whose varied intonations are soul-subduing music.
你会对我对这位神圣流浪者表达的热情微笑吗？如果你看到他，你就不会。你受过书本的熏陶和隐逸，所以有些挑剔；但这只会让你更适合欣赏这个伟大人物的非凡优点。有时我努力去发现他所拥有的是什么品质使他远远高于我所认识的任何其他人。我相信它是一种直觉的洞察力，一种快速但永不失败的判断力，一种对事物原因的洞察力，其清晰性和精确性是无与伦比的；除此之外，还有一种表达能力和一种声音，其不同的语调是征服灵魂的音乐。

August 19, 17—
2017 年 8 月 19 日——

Yesterday the stranger said to me, ‘You may easily perceive, Captain Walton, that I have suffered great and unparalleled misfortunes. I had determined at one time that the memory of these evils should die with me, but you have won me to alter my determination. You seek for knowledge and wisdom, as I once did; and I ardently hope that the gratification of your wishes may not be a serpent to sting you, as mine has been. I do not know that the relation of my disasters will be useful to you; yet, when I reflect that you are pursuing the same course, exposing yourself to the same dangers which have rendered me what I am, I imagine that you may deduce an apt moral from my tale, one that may direct you if you succeed in your undertaking and console you in case of failure. Prepare to hear of occurrences which are usually deemed marvellous. Were we among the tamer scenes of nature I might fear to encounter your unbelief, perhaps your ridicule; but many things will appear possible in these wild and mysterious regions which would provoke the laughter of those unacquainted with the ever-varied powers of nature; nor can I doubt but that my tale conveys in its series internal evidence of the truth of the events of which it is composed.’
昨天，陌生人对我说：“沃尔顿船长，你很容易看出，我遭受了巨大的、无与伦比的不幸。我曾经一度决定，这些罪恶的记忆应该与我一起消失，但你让我改变了我的决心。你寻求知识和智慧，就像我曾经做过的那样；我热切地希望，满足你的愿望不会像我的那样成为一条毒蛇来蜇你。我不知道我所描述的灾难对你有用；然而，当我想到你正在追求同样的道路，将自己暴露在同样的危险之中，正是这些危险造就了我，我想你可能会从我的故事中演绎出一个恰当的寓意，如果你成功地实现了自己的目标，它可能会指导你。承担并在失败时安慰你。准备好听到通常被认为是奇妙的事件。如果我们置身于更温和的自然风光之中，我可能会害怕遇到你的不信，也许是你的嘲笑；但是，在这些狂野而神秘的地区，许多事情似乎都是可能的，这会引起那些不熟悉自然力量的人们的笑声；我也不能怀疑，我的故事在其系列中传达了其所组成的事件的真实性的内部证据。

You may easily imagine that I was much gratified by the offered communication, yet I could not endure that he should renew his grief by a recital of his misfortunes. I felt the greatest eagerness to hear the promised narrative, partly from curiosity and partly from a strong desire to ameliorate his fate if it were in my power. I expressed these feelings in my answer.
你可能很容易想象我对所提供的沟通感到非常满意，但我无法忍受他通过讲述他的不幸来重新表达他的悲伤。我非常渴望听到所承诺的叙述，部分是出于好奇，部分是因为如果我有能力的话，我想改善他的命运。我在回答中表达了这些感受。

‘I thank you,’ he replied, ‘for your sympathy, but it is useless; my fate is nearly fulfilled. I wait but for one event, and then I shall repose in peace. I understand your feeling,’ continued he, perceiving that I wished to interrupt him; ‘but you are mistaken, my friend, if thus you will allow me to name you; nothing can alter my destiny; listen to my history, and you will perceive how irrevocably it is determined.’
“我感谢你的同情，”他回答道，“但那是没有用的；我的命运即将实现。我只等待一件事，然后我就会安息。我理解你的感受，”他继续说道，察觉到我想打断他。 “但是，我的朋友，如果你允许我这样称呼你，你就错了；没有什么可以改变我的命运；听听我的历史，你就会明白它的决定是多么不可逆转。”

He then told me that he would commence his narrative the next day when I should be at leisure. This promise drew from me the warmest thanks. I have resolved every night, when I am not imperatively occupied by my duties, to record, as nearly as possible in his own words, what he has related during the day. If I should be engaged, I will at least make notes. This manuscript will doubtless afford you the greatest pleasure; but to me, who know him and who hear it from his own lips—with what interest and sympathy shall I read it in some future day! Even now, as I commence my task, his full-toned voice swells in my ears; his lustrous eyes dwell on me with all their melancholy sweetness; I see his thin hand raised in animation, while the lineaments of his face are irradiated by the soul within. Strange and harrowing must be his story, frightful the storm which embraced the gallant vessel on its course and wrecked it—thus!
然后他告诉我，他将在第二天我有空的时候开始他的叙述。这个承诺引起了我最热烈的感谢。我决定每天晚上，当我没有必须忙于我的职责时，尽可能用他自己的话记录他白天所讲的内容。如果我应该参与，我至少会做笔记。这份手稿无疑会给您带来最大的乐趣；但对我来说，我认识他，也是从他亲口中听到的——将来的某一天，我会怀着多大的兴趣和同情心来读这本书！即使现在，当我开始我的任务时，他浑厚的声音在我耳边回响；他那双明亮的眼睛注视着我，带着忧郁的甜蜜；我看到他瘦弱的手生动地举起，而他脸上的轮廓则被内在的灵魂所照射。他的故事一定是奇怪而悲惨的，可怕的风暴席卷了正在航行中的勇敢的船只并摧毁了它——就这样！

Chapter 1
第1章

I am by birth a Genevese, and my family is one of the most distinguished of that republic. My ancestors had been for many years counsellors and syndics, and my father had filled several public situations with honour and reputation. He was respected by all who knew him for his integrity and indefatigable attention to public business. He passed his younger days perpetually occupied by the affairs of his country; a variety of circumstances had prevented his marrying early, nor was it until the decline of life that he became a husband and the father of a family.
我出生于日内瓦，我的家族是该共和国最显赫的家族之一。我的祖先多年来一直担任顾问和警长，我的父亲曾在多个公共场合担任过荣誉和声誉的职务。他因其正直和对公共事务的不懈关注而受到所有认识他的人的尊敬。他在年轻时一直忙于国家事务。种种境遇使他无法早早结婚，直到人生的衰落，他才成为丈夫和家庭的父亲。

As the circumstances of his marriage illustrate his character, I cannot refrain from relating them. One of his most intimate friends was a merchant who, from a flourishing state, fell, through numerous mischances, into poverty. This man, whose name was Beaufort, was of a proud and unbending disposition and could not bear to live in poverty and oblivion in the same country where he had formerly been distinguished for his rank and magnificence. Having paid his debts, therefore, in the most honourable manner, he retreated with his daughter to the town of Lucerne, where he lived unknown and in wretchedness. My father loved Beaufort with the truest friendship and was deeply grieved by his retreat in these unfortunate circumstances. He bitterly deplored the false pride which led his friend to a conduct so little worthy of the affection that united them. He lost no time in endeavouring to seek him out, with the hope of persuading him to begin the world again through his credit and assistance.
由于他的婚姻状况说明了他的性格，我无法避免提及这些情况。他最亲密的朋友之一是一位商人，他从繁荣的状态开始，由于无数的不幸而陷入贫困。这个名叫博福特的人性情骄傲、不屈不挠，无法忍受在他以前因地位和辉煌而闻名的那个国家生活在贫困和遗忘中。因此，在偿还了债务之后，他以最光荣的方式带着女儿撤退到卢塞恩镇，在那里他过着默默无闻、悲惨的生活。我的父亲以最真挚的友谊爱着博福特，并对他在这种不幸的情况下退却深感悲痛。他对他的朋友的虚假骄傲感到痛心疾首，这种骄傲导致他的朋友做出了如此不值得将他们团结起来的感情的行为。他不失时机地寻找他，希望通过他的信用和帮助说服他重新开始这个世界。

Beaufort had taken effectual measures to conceal himself, and it was ten months before my father discovered his abode. Overjoyed at this discovery, he hastened to the house, which was situated in a mean street near the Reuss. But when he entered, misery and despair alone welcomed him. Beaufort had saved but a very small sum of money from the wreck of his fortunes, but it was sufficient to provide him with sustenance for some months, and in the meantime he hoped to procure some respectable employment in a merchant’s house. The interval was, consequently, spent in inaction; his grief only became more deep and rankling when he had leisure for reflection, and at length it took so fast hold of his mind that at the end of three months he lay on a bed of sickness, incapable of any exertion.
博福特采取了有效的隐藏措施，十个月后我父亲才发现他的住处。他对这一发现欣喜若狂，急忙赶到位于罗伊斯河附近一条简陋街道上的房子。但当他进来时，迎接他的只有痛苦和绝望。博福特从破产中只攒下了很少的钱，但这足以让他维持几个月的生活，同时他希望在商人家里找到一份体面的工作。结果，这段时间就无所事事地度过了。当他有时间思考时，他的悲伤只会变得更加深沉和痛苦，最终它如此迅速地占据了他的思想，以至于三个月后他躺在病床上，无法做任何努力。

His daughter attended him with the greatest tenderness, but she saw with despair that their little fund was rapidly decreasing and that there was no other prospect of support. But Caroline Beaufort possessed a mind of an uncommon mould, and her courage rose to support her in her adversity. She procured plain work; she plaited straw and by various means contrived to earn a pittance scarcely sufficient to support life.
他的女儿非常温柔地照顾他，但她绝望地看到他们的一点钱正在迅速减少，而且没有其他的支持前景。但卡罗琳·博福特有着不寻常的头脑，她在逆境中鼓起勇气支持她。她找到了一份简单的工作；她用稻草编辫子，想方设法挣点微薄的钱，勉强维持生活。

Several months passed in this manner. Her father grew worse; her time was more entirely occupied in attending him; her means of subsistence decreased; and in the tenth month her father died in her arms, leaving her an orphan and a beggar. This last blow overcame her, and she knelt by Beaufort’s coffin weeping bitterly, when my father entered the chamber. He came like a protecting spirit to the poor girl, who committed herself to his care; and after the interment of his friend he conducted her to Geneva and placed her under the protection of a relation. Two years after this event Caroline became his wife.
就这样，几个月过去了。她父亲的病情恶化了。她的时间更多地花在照顾他上。她的生活资料减少了；第十个月，她的父亲死在她怀里，留下她成为孤儿和乞丐。这最后的打击压倒了她，当我父亲走进房间时，她跪在博福特的棺材旁痛哭。他就像一个保护神一样来到这个可怜的女孩身边，让她全心全意地照顾她。在他的朋友安葬后，他将她带到了日内瓦，并将她置于一位亲戚的保护之下。此事发生两年后，卡罗琳成为了他的妻子。

There was a considerable difference between the ages of my parents, but this circumstance seemed to unite them only closer in bonds of devoted affection. There was a sense of justice in my father’s upright mind which rendered it necessary that he should approve highly to love strongly. Perhaps during former years he had suffered from the late-discovered unworthiness of one beloved and so was disposed to set a greater value on tried worth. There was a show of gratitude and worship in his attachment to my mother, differing wholly from the doting fondness of age, for it was inspired by reverence for her virtues and a desire to be the means of, in some degree, recompensing her for the sorrows she had endured, but which gave inexpressible grace to his behaviour to her. Everything was made to yield to her wishes and her convenience. He strove to shelter her, as a fair exotic is sheltered by the gardener, from every rougher wind and to surround her with all that could tend to excite pleasurable emotion in her soft and benevolent mind. Her health, and even the tranquillity of her hitherto constant spirit, had been shaken by what she had gone through. During the two years that had elapsed previous to their marriage my father had gradually relinquished all his public functions; and immediately after their union they sought the pleasant climate of Italy, and the change of scene and interest attendant on a tour through that land of wonders, as a restorative for her weakened frame.
我父母的年龄相差很大，但这种情况似乎使他们的感情纽带更加紧密。父亲正直的心灵里有一种正义感，所以他必须高度认可才能强烈地去爱。也许在过去的几年里，他因为后来发现自己所爱的人不值得而遭受痛苦，因此倾向于更加看重尝试过的价值。他对我母亲的依恋中流露出感激和崇拜，这与年老时的溺爱完全不同，因为他对母亲的美德怀有敬意，并渴望在某种程度上补偿她的付出。她忍受了悲伤，但这却给他对她的行为带来了难以言喻的恩典。一切都是为了满足她的愿望和她的方便。他努力保护她，就像园丁保护美丽的异域风情一样，让她免受狂风的侵袭，并用一切能够在她柔软仁慈的心灵中激发愉悦情绪的东西包围着她。她的健康，甚至她一直以来的平静精神，都因她所经历的事情而动摇了。在他们结婚前的两年里，我父亲逐渐放弃了所有的公共职能。他们结婚后不久，他们就寻求意大利宜人的气候，以及在这片神奇的土地上旅行所带来的场景和兴趣的变化，作为她虚弱的身体的恢复。

From Italy they visited Germany and France. I, their eldest child, was born at Naples, and as an infant accompanied them in their rambles. I remained for several years their only child. Much as they were attached to each other, they seemed to draw inexhaustible stores of affection from a very mine of love to bestow them upon me. My mother’s tender caresses and my father’s smile of benevolent pleasure while regarding me are my first recollections. I was their plaything and their idol, and something better—their child, the innocent and helpless creature bestowed on them by heaven, whom to bring up to good, and whose future lot it was in their hands to direct to happiness or misery, according as they fulfilled their duties towards me. With this deep consciousness of what they owed towards the being to which they had given life, added to the active spirit of tenderness that animated both, it may be imagined that while during every hour of my infant life I received a lesson of patience, of charity, and of self-control, I was so guided by a silken cord that all seemed but one train of enjoyment to me.
他们从意大利访问了德国和法国。我，他们的长子，出生在那不勒斯，婴儿时期就陪伴他们漫步。几年来，我一直是他们唯一的孩子。尽管他们彼此依恋，但他们似乎从爱的宝藏中汲取了无穷无尽的感情来赐给我。母亲温柔的爱抚和父亲看着我时充满慈爱和喜悦的微笑是我最初的记忆。我是他们的玩物，他们的偶像，而且是更好的东西——他们的孩子，上天赐予他们的天真无助的生物，他们要养育他们向善，而他们未来的命运则掌握在他们的手中，引导他们走向幸福或痛苦。因为他们履行了对我的职责。有了这种对他们赋予生命的存在的深刻认识，再加上激发两者活力的积极温柔精神，可以想象，在我婴儿生活的每个小时里，我都接受了耐心的教训，慈善、自我控制，我被一根丝绳所引导，对我来说，这一切似乎只是一列享受。

For a long time I was their only care. My mother had much desired to have a daughter, but I continued their single offspring. When I was about five years old, while making an excursion beyond the frontiers of Italy, they passed a week on the shores of the Lake of Como. Their benevolent disposition often made them enter the cottages of the poor. This, to my mother, was more than a duty; it was a necessity, a passion—remembering what she had suffered, and how she had been relieved—for her to act in her turn the guardian angel to the afflicted. During one of their walks a poor cot in the foldings of a vale attracted their notice as being singularly disconsolate, while the number of half-clothed children gathered about it spoke of penury in its worst shape. One day, when my father had gone by himself to Milan, my mother, accompanied by me, visited this abode. She found a peasant and his wife, hard working, bent down by care and labour, distributing a scanty meal to five hungry babes. Among these there was one which attracted my mother far above all the rest. She appeared of a different stock. The four others were dark-eyed, hardy little vagrants; this child was thin and very fair. Her hair was the brightest living gold, and despite the poverty of her clothing, seemed to set a crown of distinction on her head. Her brow was clear and ample, her blue eyes cloudless, and her lips and the moulding of her face so expressive of sensibility and sweetness that none could behold her without looking on her as of a distinct species, a being heaven-sent, and bearing a celestial stamp in all her features.
很长一段时间，我是他们唯一的照顾。我的母亲非常渴望有一个女儿，但我却继续他们的单身后代。当我大约五岁的时候，在一次跨越意大利边境的旅行中，他们在科莫湖畔度过了一周。他们的仁慈性格常常使他们走进穷人的小屋。对我母亲来说，这不仅仅是一种义务；更是一种责任。对她来说，将守护天使变成受苦者的守护天使是必要的，是一种激情——记住她所遭受的痛苦，以及她是如何得到解脱的。有一次他们散步时，山谷褶皱处的一张简陋的简易床引起了他们的注意，因为它异常令人沮丧，而聚集在它周围的许多半裸的孩子则说明了最糟糕的贫困状况。有一天，父亲独自去米兰，母亲在我的陪同下参观了这处住所。她发现一个农民和他的妻子正在辛勤地工作，在照顾和劳动中弯下腰，给五个饥饿的婴儿分发少量的食物。其中，有一件事情最吸引我的母亲。她看起来与众不同。另外四个人都是黑眼睛、坚强的小流浪汉。这孩子很瘦，而且很白皙。她的头发是最闪亮的金色，尽管她的衣服简陋，但似乎在她的头上戴了一顶尊贵的王冠。她的眉毛清晰而宽大，她的蓝眼睛清澈见底，她的嘴唇和脸型都表现出感性和甜美，任何人看到她都会觉得她是一个独特的物种，一个天赐的、有气质的人。她的所有特征都带有天国的印记。

The peasant woman, perceiving that my mother fixed eyes of wonder and admiration on this lovely girl, eagerly communicated her history. She was not her child, but the daughter of a Milanese nobleman. Her mother was a German and had died on giving her birth. The infant had been placed with these good people to nurse: they were better off then. They had not been long married, and their eldest child was but just born. The father of their charge was one of those Italians nursed in the memory of the antique glory of Italy—one among the *schiavi ognor frementi*, who exerted himself to obtain the liberty of his country. He became the victim of its weakness. Whether he had died or still lingered in the dungeons of Austria was not known. His property was confiscated; his child became an orphan and a beggar. She continued with her foster parents and bloomed in their rude abode, fairer than a garden rose among dark-leaved brambles.
农妇察觉到母亲用惊奇和钦佩的目光注视着这个可爱的女孩，就急切地讲述了她的故事。她不是她的孩子，而是一位米兰贵族的女儿。她的母亲是德国人，在生下她时去世。婴儿被安置在这些好人身边来护理：那时他们的处境更好了。他们结婚时间不长，最大的孩子刚刚出生。他们的父亲是一位怀念意大利古代辉煌的意大利人，他是*斯基亚维·奥格诺·弗雷门蒂*中的一员，他为获得国家的自由而奋斗。他成为其弱点的受害者。他是死了，还是仍在奥地利的地牢里徘徊，不得而知。他的财产被没收；他的孩子成了孤儿和乞丐。她继续和她的养父母在一起，在他们简陋的住所里绽放，比黑叶荆棘丛中的花园玫瑰还要美丽。

When my father returned from Milan, he found playing with me in the hall of our villa a child fairer than pictured cherub— a creature who seemed to shed radiance from her looks and whose form and motions were lighter than the chamois of the hills. The apparition was soon explained. With his permission my mother prevailed on her rustic guardians to yield their charge to her. They were fond of the sweet orphan. Her presence had seemed a blessing to them, but it would be unfair to her to keep her in poverty and want when Providence afforded her such powerful protection. They consulted their village priest, and the result was that Elizabeth Lavenza became the inmate of my parents’ house— my more than sister—the beautiful and adored companion of all my occupations and my pleasures.
当我父亲从米兰回来时，他发现在我们别墅的大厅里和我一起玩耍的孩子比照片上的小天使还要美丽——这种生物似乎从她的外表中散发出光芒，其体形和动作比山上的麂皮还要轻盈。这个现象很快就得到了解释。在他的允许下，我母亲说服了她乡下的监护人将他们的职责交给了她。他们很喜欢这个可爱的孤儿。她的出现对他们来说似乎是一种祝福，但当上帝为她提供如此强大的保护时，让她陷入贫困和匮乏对她来说是不公平的。他们咨询了乡村牧师，结果是伊丽莎白·拉文扎成为了我父母家里的住户——不仅仅是我的妹妹——她是我所有职业和快乐的美丽和受人爱戴的伴侣。

Everyone loved Elizabeth. The passionate and almost reverential attachment with which all regarded her became, while I shared it, my pride and my delight. On the evening previous to her being brought to my home, my mother had said playfully, ‘I have a pretty present for my Victor— tomorrow he shall have it.’ And when, on the morrow, she presented Elizabeth to me as her promised gift, I, with childish seriousness, interpreted her words literally and looked upon Elizabeth as mine—mine to protect, love, and cherish. All praises bestowed on her I received as made to a possession of my own. We called each other familiarly by the name of cousin. No word, no expression could body forth the kind of relation in which she stood to me—my more than sister, since till death she was to be mine only.
每个人都喜欢伊丽莎白。所有人对她的热情和近乎虔诚的依恋，在我分享的同时，也变成了我的骄傲和喜悦。在她被带到我家的前一天晚上，我母亲开玩笑地说：“我有一件漂亮的礼物要送给我的维克多——明天他就会收到它。”第二天，她按照她的承诺把伊丽莎白送给了我。礼物，我带着孩子般的严肃，从字面上解释了她的话，并将伊丽莎白视为我的——我的保护，爱和珍惜。我收到的所有对她的赞美都像是我自己的财产。我们亲切地称呼对方为表弟的名字。任何言语、任何表达都无法体现她与我的关系——她不仅仅是我的妹妹，因为直到死亡她都只属于我。

Chapter 2
第2章

We were brought up together; there was not quite a year difference in our ages. I need not say that we were strangers to any species of disunion or dispute. Harmony was the soul of our companionship, and the diversity and contrast that subsisted in our characters drew us nearer together. Elizabeth was of a calmer and more concentrated disposition; but, with all my ardour, I was capable of a more intense application and was more deeply smitten with the thirst for knowledge. She busied herself with following the aerial creations of the poets; and in the majestic and wondrous scenes which surrounded our Swiss home—the sublime shapes of the mountains, the changes of the seasons, tempest and calm, the silence of winter, and the life and turbulence of our Alpine summers—she found ample scope for admiration and delight. While my companion contemplated with a serious and satisfied spirit the magnificent appearances of things, I delighted in investigating their causes. The world was to me a secret which I desired to divine. Curiosity, earnest research to learn the hidden laws of nature, gladness akin to rapture, as they were unfolded to me, are among the earliest sensations I can remember.
我们是一起长大的；我们的年龄相差不大。不用说，我们对任何形式的不和或争端都是陌生的。和谐是我们友谊的灵魂，我们性格中存在的多样性和对比使我们更加亲近。伊丽莎白性格比较平静，也比较专注。但是，尽管我充满热情，但我能够更加强烈地应用，并且对知识的渴求更加强烈。她忙于追踪诗人的空中创作；在我们瑞士家乡周围雄伟而奇妙的景色中——山脉的雄伟形状、季节的变化、暴风雨和平静、冬天的寂静、阿尔卑斯山夏天的生机和动荡——她发现了充足的空间钦佩和欣喜。当我的同伴以严肃而满足的精神思考事物的壮丽外表时，我却乐于探究它们的原因。世界对我来说是一个我渴望探知的秘密。好奇心、对自然隐藏规律的认真研究、近乎狂喜的喜悦，当它们向我展开时，是我记忆中最早的感觉之一。

On the birth of a second son, my junior by seven years, my parents gave up entirely their wandering life and fixed themselves in their native country. We possessed a house in Geneva, and a campagne on Belrive, the eastern shore of the lake, at the distance of rather more than a league from the city. We resided principally in the latter, and the lives of my parents were passed in considerable seclusion. It was my temper to avoid a crowd and to attach myself fervently to a few. I was indifferent, therefore, to my school-fellows in general; but I united myself in the bonds of the closest friendship to one among them. Henry Clerval was the son of a merchant of Geneva. He was a boy of singular talent and fancy. He loved enterprise, hardship, and even danger for its own sake. He was deeply read in books of chivalry and romance. He composed heroic songs and began to write many a tale of enchantment and knightly adventure. He tried to make us act plays and to enter into masquerades, in which the characters were drawn from the heroes of Roncesvalles, of the Round Table of King Arthur, and the chivalrous train who shed their blood to redeem the holy sepulchre from the hands of the infidels.
当第二个儿子（比我小七岁）出生时，我的父母完全放弃了漂泊的生活，定居在自己的祖国。我们在日内瓦拥有一栋房子，在湖东岸贝尔里夫拥有一处乡村，距离城市超过一里格。我们主要居住在后者，我父母的生活相当隐秘。我的性格就是避开人群而热衷于少数人。因此，我对我的同学们普遍漠不关心。但我与其中一位以最亲密的友谊联系在一起。亨利·克莱瓦尔是日内瓦商人的儿子。他是一个才华横溢、想象力丰富的男孩。他热爱进取，热爱艰辛，甚至热爱冒险。他对武侠小说和言情小说都有深入的阅读。他创作了英雄歌曲，并开始撰写许多魔法和骑士冒险的故事。他试图让我们表演戏剧并参加化装舞会，其中的角色来自龙塞斯瓦莱斯的英雄，亚瑟王圆桌会议的英雄，以及为从国王手中赎回圣墓而流血的骑士队伍。异教徒。

No human being could have passed a happier childhood than myself. My parents were possessed by the very spirit of kindness and indulgence. We felt that they were not the tyrants to rule our lot according to their caprice, but the agents and creators of all the many delights which we enjoyed. When I mingled with other families I distinctly discerned how peculiarly fortunate my lot was, and gratitude assisted the development of filial love.
没有人能比我度过更快乐的童年。我的父母充满了仁慈和宽容的精神。我们觉得他们不是随心所欲地统治我们命运的暴君，而是我们享受的所有快乐的代理人和创造者。当我与其他家庭交往时，我清楚地认识到自己的命运是多么的幸运，感恩之心有助于培养孝心。

My temper was sometimes violent, and my passions vehement; but by some law in my temperature they were turned not towards childish pursuits but to an eager desire to learn, and not to learn all things indiscriminately. I confess that neither the structure of languages, nor the code of governments, nor the politics of various states possessed attractions for me. It was the secrets of heaven and earth that I desired to learn; and whether it was the outward substance of things or the inner spirit of nature and the mysterious soul of man that occupied me, still my inquiries were directed to the metaphysical, or in its highest sense, the physical secrets of the world.
我的脾气有时很暴躁，我的激情也很强烈；但根据我的体温的某种规律，他们不会转向幼稚的追求，而是转向渴望学习，而不是不加区别地学习所有东西。我承认，无论是语言的结构，还是政府的法典，还是各国的政治，都对我没有吸引力。我所欲知的是天地之奥秘；无论是事物的外在本质，还是自然的内在精神和人类神秘的灵魂，我的探究仍然是针对形而上学的，或者从最高意义上来说，是世界的物理秘密。

Meanwhile Clerval occupied himself, so to speak, with the moral relations of things. The busy stage of life, the virtues of heroes, and the actions of men were his theme; and his hope and his dream was to become one among those whose names are recorded in story as the gallant and adventurous benefactors of our species. The saintly soul of Elizabeth shone like a shrine-dedicated lamp in our peaceful home. Her sympathy was ours; her smile, her soft voice, the sweet glance of her celestial eyes, were ever there to bless and animate us. She was the living spirit of love to soften and attract; I might have become sullen in my study, through the ardour of my nature, but that she was there to subdue me to a semblance of her own gentleness. And Clerval—could aught ill entrench on the noble spirit of Clerval? Yet he might not have been so perfectly humane, so thoughtful in his generosity, so full of kindness and tenderness amidst his passion for adventurous exploit, had she not unfolded to him the real loveliness of beneficence and made the doing good the end and aim of his soaring ambition.
与此同时，可以说，克莱瓦尔全神贯注于事物的道德关系。忙碌的人生阶段、英雄的美德、男人的行为是他的主题；他的希望和梦想是成为那些名字被记录在故事中的人中的一员，成为我们人类勇敢和冒险的恩人。伊丽莎白的圣洁灵魂就像一盏神社专用的灯在我们宁静的家里闪闪发光。我们也同情她；她的微笑，她柔和的声音，她天眼的甜蜜目光，一直在祝福我们，激励我们。她是爱的活泼精灵，可以软化和吸引；由于我天性的热情，我可能会在学习中变得闷闷不乐，但她在那里是为了让我表现出她自己的温柔。还有克莱瓦尔——难道还有什么会损害克莱瓦尔的高贵精神吗？然而，如果她没有向他展示仁慈的真正可爱，并把行善作为他的目的和目的，他可能不会如此完美的人道，如此慷慨的体贴，在他对冒险事业的热情中如此充满仁慈和温柔。他那高涨的野心。

I feel exquisite pleasure in dwelling on the recollections of childhood, before misfortune had tainted my mind and changed its bright visions of extensive usefulness into gloomy and narrow reflections upon self. Besides, in drawing the picture of my early days, I also record those events which led, by insensible steps, to my after tale of misery, for when I would account to myself for the birth of that passion which afterward ruled my destiny I find it arise, like a mountain river, from ignoble and almost forgotten sources; but, swelling as it proceeded, it became the torrent which, in its course, has swept away all my hopes and joys. Natural philosophy is the genius that has regulated my fate; I desire, therefore, in this narration, to state those facts which led to my predilection for that science. When I was thirteen years of age we all went on a party of pleasure to the baths near Thonon; the inclemency of the weather obliged us to remain a day confined to the inn. In this house I chanced to find a volume of the works of Cornelius Agrippa. I opened it with apathy; the theory which he attempts to demonstrate and the wonderful facts which he relates soon changed this feeling into enthusiasm. A new light seemed to dawn upon my mind, and bounding with joy, I communicated my discovery to my father. My father looked carelessly at the title page of my book and said, ‘Ah! Cornelius Agrippa! My dear Victor, do not waste your time upon this; it is sad trash.’
在不幸玷污我的心灵，将其广泛有用的光明愿景变成对自我的阴暗和狭隘反思之前，我在沉思童年的回忆中感到无比的快乐。此外，在描绘我早年生活的过程中，我还记录了那些不知不觉中导致我后来的悲惨故事的事件，因为当我向自己解释后来主宰我命运的激情的诞生时，我发现它就像山间河流一样，源自卑鄙且几乎被遗忘的源头；但是，随着它的发展，它变成了洪流，在它的过程中，席卷了我所有的希望和欢乐。自然哲学是调节我命运的天才；因此，我希望在这篇叙述中陈述那些导致我偏爱这门科学的事实。当我十三岁的时候，我们全家去托农附近的浴场参加了一次快乐的聚会；恶劣的天气迫使我们在旅馆里待了一天。在这所房子里，我偶然发现了一卷科尼利厄斯·阿格里帕的作品。我冷漠地打开它；他试图论证的理论和他所讲述的奇妙事实很快就把这种感觉变成了热情。我的脑海中似乎出现了新的曙光，我高兴地跳了起来，把我的发现告诉了父亲。父亲漫不经心地看着我书的扉页，说：‘啊！科尼利厄斯·阿格里帕！我亲爱的维克多，不要在这上面浪费你的时间；这是可悲的垃圾。

If, instead of this remark, my father had taken the pains to explain to me that the principles of Agrippa had been entirely exploded and that a modern system of science had been introduced which possessed much greater powers than the ancient, because the powers of the latter were chimerical, while those of the former were real and practical, under such circumstances I should certainly have thrown Agrippa aside and have contented my imagination, warmed as it was, by returning with greater ardour to my former studies. It is even possible that the train of my ideas would never have received the fatal impulse that led to my ruin. But the cursory glance my father had taken of my volume by no means assured me that he was acquainted with its contents, and I continued to read with the greatest avidity. When I returned home my first care was to procure the whole works of this author, and afterwards of Paracelsus and Albertus Magnus. I read and studied the wild fancies of these writers with delight; they appeared to me treasures known to few besides myself. I have described myself as always having been imbued with a fervent longing to penetrate the secrets of nature. In spite of the intense labour and wonderful discoveries of modern philosophers, I always came from my studies discontented and unsatisfied. Sir Isaac Newton is said to have avowed that he felt like a child picking up shells beside the great and unexplored ocean of truth. Those of his successors in each branch of natural philosophy with whom I was acquainted appeared even to my boy’s apprehensions as tyros engaged in the same pursuit.
如果我父亲没有说这句话，而是煞费苦心地向我解释阿格里帕的原理已经完全被推翻，并且引入了一种现代科学体系，它拥有比古代科学体系更强大的力量，因为科学的力量后者是空想的，而前者是真实的和实际的，在这种情况下，我当然应该把阿格里帕抛在一边，并通过以更大的热情回到我以前的学习来满足我的想象力，尽管它已经温暖了。甚至有可能我的一系列想法永远不会受到导致我毁灭的致命冲动。但我父亲粗略地浏览了我的书，但这并不能让我确信他熟悉其中的内容，我继续以最大的热情阅读。当我回到家时，我首先关心的是购买这位作者的全部作品，然后是帕拉塞尔苏斯和阿尔伯特·马格努斯的作品。我欣喜地阅读和研究了这些作家的疯狂幻想。在我看来，它们就像是除了我自己之外很少有人知道的宝藏。我形容自己始终充满着探究自然秘密的强烈渴望。尽管现代哲学家付出了辛勤的劳动和奇妙的发现，但我总是对我的研究感到不满和不满足。据说艾萨克·牛顿爵士曾坦言，他感觉就像一个孩子在伟大的、未经探索的真理海洋旁捡贝壳。我所认识的他在自然哲学各个分支的继承者们甚至在我儿子看来，就像从事同样追求的新手一样。

The untaught peasant beheld the elements around him and was acquainted with their practical uses. The most learned philosopher knew little more. He had partially unveiled the face of Nature, but her immortal lineaments were still a wonder and a mystery. He might dissect, anatomize, and give names; but, not to speak of a final cause, causes in their secondary and tertiary grades were utterly unknown to him. I had gazed upon the fortifications and impediments that seemed to keep human beings from entering the citadel of nature, and rashly and ignorantly I had repined.
未受过教育的农民观察了他周围的元素并熟悉了它们的实际用途。最有学问的哲学家知道的也很少。他已经部分揭开了大自然的面容，但她不朽的面容仍然是一个奇迹和一个谜。他可以解剖、解剖并命名；但不说最终的原因，就连他们中学、大学的原因他也全然不知道。我凝视着似乎阻止人类进入自然堡垒的防御工事和障碍，我轻率而无知地抱怨起来。

But here were books, and here were men who had penetrated deeper and knew more. I took their word for all that they averred, and I became their disciple. It may appear strange that such should arise in the eighteenth century; but while I followed the routine of education in the schools of Geneva, I was, to a great degree, self-taught with regard to my favourite studies. My father was not scientific, and I was left to struggle with a child’s blindness, added to a student’s thirst for knowledge. Under the guidance of my new preceptors I entered with the greatest diligence into the search of the philosopher’s stone and the elixir of life; but the latter soon obtained my undivided attention. Wealth was an inferior object, but what glory would attend the discovery if I could banish disease from the human frame and render man invulnerable to any but a violent death! Nor were these my only visions. The raising of ghosts or devils was a promise liberally accorded by my favourite authors, the fulfillment of which I most eagerly sought; and if my incantations were always unsuccessful, I attributed the failure rather to my own inexperience and mistake than to a want of skill or fidelity in my instructors. And thus for a time I was occupied by exploded systems, mingling, like an unadept, a thousand contradictory theories and floundering desperately in a very slough of multifarious knowledge, guided by an ardent imagination and childish reasoning, till an accident again changed the current of my ideas. When I was about fifteen years old we had retired to our house near Belrive, when we witnessed a most violent and terrible thunderstorm. It advanced from behind the mountains of Jura, and the thunder burst at once with frightful loudness from various quarters of the heavens. I remained, while the storm lasted, watching its progress with curiosity and delight. As I stood at the door, on a sudden I beheld a stream of fire issue from an old and beautiful oak which stood about twenty yards from our house; and so soon as the dazzling light vanished, the oak had disappeared, and nothing remained but a blasted stump. When we visited it the next morning, we found the tree shattered in a singular manner. It was not splintered by the shock, but entirely reduced to thin ribbons of wood. I never beheld anything so utterly destroyed.
但这里有书籍，这里有更深入、了解更多的人。我相信他们所说的一切，并成为他们的门徒。这种事发生在 18 世纪，可能会显得很奇怪。虽然我在日内瓦学校接受常规教育，但在很大程度上，我最喜欢的学习是自学的。我的父亲不懂科学，而我则不得不与孩子的失明作斗争，这增加了学生对知识的渴望。在我的新导师的指导下，我以最大的努力开始寻找点金石和长生不老药。但后者很快引起了我的全神贯注。财富是一个低等的物体，但是如果我能够从人体中消除疾病，使人类除了暴力死亡之外不会受到任何伤害，那么这个发现将是多么荣耀啊！这些并不是我唯一的愿景。唤起鬼魂或魔鬼是我最喜欢的作家慷慨许下的承诺，也是我最渴望实现的。如果我的咒语总是不成功，我会将失败归咎于我自己的经验不足和错误，而不是归咎于我的导师缺乏技巧或忠诚。因此，有一段时间，我被爆炸性的系统所占据，像一个不熟练的人一样，混合着上千种相互矛盾的理论，在热情的想象力和幼稚的推理的引导下，在五花八门的知识泥沼中绝望地挣扎，直到一场意外再次改变了潮流。我的想法。当我大约十五岁时，我们退休到贝尔里夫附近的房子，当时我们目睹了一场最猛烈、最可怕的雷暴。它从汝拉山脉的后方袭来，雷霆立刻从天空的各个角落爆发出来，发出可怕的响声。 暴风雨持续期间，我留下来，怀着好奇和喜悦的心情观察着它的进展。当我站在门口时，突然我看到一股火流从距离我们房子大约二十码的一棵古老而美丽的橡树中喷出；耀眼的光芒一消失，橡树就消失了，只剩下一根枯萎的树桩。当我们第二天早上去拜访它时，我们发现这棵树以一种奇怪的方式破碎了。它并没有被冲击击碎，而是完全变成了细木条。我从来没有见过任何东西被如此彻底地摧毁。

Before this I was not unacquainted with the more obvious laws of electricity. On this occasion a man of great research in natural philosophy was with us, and excited by this catastrophe, he entered on the explanation of a theory which he had formed on the subject of electricity and galvanism, which was at once new and astonishing to me. All that he said threw greatly into the shade Cornelius Agrippa, Albertus Magnus, and Paracelsus, the lords of my imagination; but by some fatality the overthrow of these men disinclined me to pursue my accustomed studies. It seemed to me as if nothing would or could ever be known. All that had so long engaged my attention suddenly grew despicable. By one of those caprices of the mind which we are perhaps most subject to in early youth, I at once gave up my former occupations, set down natural history and all its progeny as a deformed and abortive creation, and entertained the greatest disdain for a would-be science which could never even step within the threshold of real knowledge. In this mood of mind I betook myself to the mathematics and the branches of study appertaining to that science as being built upon secure foundations, and so worthy of my consideration.
在此之前，我对更明显的电定律并不陌生。这次，一位对自然哲学有伟大研究的人和我们在一起，他对这场灾难感到兴奋，开始解释他在电和流电学主题上形成的理论，这对我来说是新的和令人惊讶的。他所说的一切都让我想象中的领主科尼利厄斯·阿格里帕、阿尔贝图斯·马格努斯和帕拉塞尔苏斯黯然失色。但不幸的是，这些人的推翻使我无法继续我惯常的研究。在我看来，似乎什么都不会或永远不可能被知道。长期以来吸引我注意力的一切突然变得卑鄙。由于我们在青年时代可能最容易受到思想反复无常的影响，我立即放弃了以前的职业，将博物学及其所有后代视为畸形和流产的创造物，并对自然历史表示最大的蔑视。未来的科学甚至永远无法迈入真正知识的门槛。在这种心态下，我开始研究数学和与该科学相关的研究分支，因为它们建立在牢固的基础上，因此值得我考虑。

Thus strangely are our souls constructed, and by such slight ligaments are we bound to prosperity or ruin. When I look back, it seems to me as if this almost miraculous change of inclination and will was the immediate suggestion of the guardian angel of my life—the last effort made by the spirit of preservation to avert the storm that was even then hanging in the stars and ready to envelop me. Her victory was announced by an unusual tranquillity and gladness of soul which followed the relinquishing of my ancient and latterly tormenting studies. It was thus that I was to be taught to associate evil with their prosecution, happiness with their disregard.
我们的灵魂就是这样奇怪地构造出来的，我们的繁荣或毁灭就由如此微小的韧带所束缚。当我回首往事时，在我看来，这种倾向和意志近乎奇迹般的变化似乎是我生命守护天使的直接暗示——保护精神为避免当时就已经悬而未决的风暴所做的最后努力。星星准备包围我。在我放弃了古老而近来折磨人的研究之后，我的灵魂出现了一种不同寻常的平静和快乐，宣告了她的胜利。正是这样，我被教导将邪恶与他们的起诉联系起来，将幸福与他们的漠视联系起来。

It was a strong effort of the spirit of good, but it was ineffectual. Destiny was too potent, and her immutable laws had decreed my utter and terrible destruction.
这是善良精神的强烈努力，但没有效果。命运太强大了，她那不可改变的法则已经注定了我彻底而可怕的毁灭。

Chapter 3
第3章

When I had attained the age of seventeen my parents resolved that I should become a student at the university of Ingolstadt. I had hitherto attended the schools of Geneva, but my father thought it necessary for the completion of my education that I should be made acquainted with other customs than those of my native country. My departure was therefore fixed at an early date, but before the day resolved upon could arrive, the first misfortune of my life occurred—an omen, as it were, of my future misery. Elizabeth had caught the scarlet fever; her illness was severe, and she was in the greatest danger. During her illness many arguments had been urged to persuade my mother to refrain from attending upon her. She had at first yielded to our entreaties, but when she heard that the life of her favourite was menaced, she could no longer control her anxiety. She attended her sickbed; her watchful attentions triumphed over the malignity of the distemper—Elizabeth was saved, but the consequences of this imprudence were fatal to her preserver. On the third day my mother sickened; her fever was accompanied by the most alarming symptoms, and the looks of her medical attendants prognosticated the worst event. On her deathbed the fortitude and benignity of this best of women did not desert her. She joined the hands of Elizabeth and myself. ‘My children,’ she said, ‘my firmest hopes of future happiness were placed on the prospect of your union. This expectation will now be the consolation of your father. Elizabeth, my love, you must supply my place to my younger children. Alas! I regret that I am taken from you; and, happy and beloved as I have been, is it not hard to quit you all? But these are not thoughts befitting me; I will endeavour to resign myself cheerfully to death and will indulge a hope of meeting you in another world.’
当我十七岁时，我的父母决定我应该成为因戈尔施塔特大学的一名学生。迄今为止，我一直在日内瓦的学校上学，但我的父亲认为，为了完成学业，我有必要熟悉祖国以外的其他习俗。因此，我的出发日期被提前定下来，但在决定的那一天到来之前，我一生中的第一个不幸发生了——这可以说是我未来痛苦的预兆。伊丽莎白染上了猩红热。她的病很重，处于最大的危险之中。在她生病期间，有人提出了许多论点，以说服我母亲不要照顾她。起初她屈服于我们的恳求，但当她听说她最爱的人的生命受到威胁时，她再也无法控制自己的焦虑。她照顾病床；她的警惕性战胜了瘟疫的恶性——伊丽莎白得救了，但这种轻率的后果对她的保护者来说却是致命的。第三天，我母亲病了。她的发烧伴随着最令人震惊的症状，而她的医护人员的表情预示着最糟糕的情况。在她临终前，这位最好的女性的坚韧和善良并没有抛弃她。她牵起伊丽莎白和我的手。 “我的孩子们，”她说，“我对未来幸福最坚定的希望寄托在你们结合的前景上。这种期望现在将成为你父亲的安慰。伊丽莎白，我的爱人，你必须把我的位置让给我年幼的孩子们。唉!我很遗憾我被从你身边带走；而且，尽管我一直很快乐，也很受人爱戴，但离开你们大家不是很难吗？ 但这些想法不适合我；我会尽力高高兴兴地听天由命，并寄希望于在另一个世界遇见你。’

She died calmly, and her countenance expressed affection even in death. I need not describe the feelings of those whose dearest ties are rent by that most irreparable evil, the void that presents itself to the soul, and the despair that is exhibited on the countenance. It is so long before the mind can persuade itself that she whom we saw every day and whose very existence appeared a part of our own can have departed forever—that the brightness of a beloved eye can have been extinguished and the sound of a voice so familiar and dear to the ear can be hushed, never more to be heard. These are the reflections of the first days; but when the lapse of time proves the reality of the evil, then the actual bitterness of grief commences. Yet from whom has not that rude hand rent away some dear connection? And why should I describe a sorrow which all have felt, and must feel? The time at length arrives when grief is rather an indulgence than a necessity; and the smile that plays upon the lips, although it may be deemed a sacrilege, is not banished. My mother was dead, but we had still duties which we ought to perform; we must continue our course with the rest and learn to think ourselves fortunate whilst one remains whom the spoiler has not seized. My departure for Ingolstadt, which had been deferred by these events, was now again determined upon. I obtained from my father a respite of some weeks. It appeared to me sacrilege so soon to leave the repose, akin to death, of the house of mourning and to rush into the thick of life. I was new to sorrow, but it did not the less alarm me. I was unwilling to quit the sight of those that remained to me, and above all, I desired to see my sweet Elizabeth in some degree consoled.
她死得很平静，死的时候脸上也流露出慈爱。我不需要描述那些最亲密的纽带被最无法挽回的邪恶撕裂的人的感受，他们的灵魂呈现出空虚，脸上流露出绝望。过了很长时间，心灵才说服自己相信我们每天见到的她，她的存在本身就是我们自己的一部分，她可能已经永远离开了——心爱的眼睛的光芒可能已经消失，声音也可能已经消失了。耳熟能详的声音可以安静下来，再也听不到。这些是第一天的反思；但当时间的流逝证明了邪恶的真实存在时，悲伤的真正痛苦就开始了。然而，那只粗鲁的手没有从谁手中夺走一些亲密的联系呢？我为什么要描述一种所有人都曾感受过、也必须感受到的悲伤？悲伤不再是一种必然，而是一种放纵的时刻终于到来了。嘴唇上的微笑虽然可能被认为是一种亵渎，但并没有消失。我的母亲去世了，但我们还有应该履行的职责；我们必须与其他人一起继续我们的路线，并学会在还有人没有被破坏者抓住的时候认为自己是幸运的。我因这些事件而推迟前往因戈尔施塔特的行程，现在又决定了。我从父亲那里获得了几周的喘息时间。在我看来，这么快就离开了哀悼之家的安宁，就像死亡一样，冲进了生活的最深处，这似乎是一种亵渎。我对悲伤还很陌生，但这并没有减轻我的惊慌。我不愿意离开那些留在我身边的人，最重要的是，我希望看到我可爱的伊丽莎白得到某种程度的安慰。

She indeed veiled her grief and strove to act the comforter to us all. She looked steadily on life and assumed its duties with courage and zeal. She devoted herself to those whom she had been taught to call her uncle and cousins. Never was she so enchanting as at this time, when she recalled the sunshine of her smiles and spent them upon us. She forgot even her own regret in her endeavours to make us forget.
她确实掩饰了她的悲伤，并努力充当我们所有人的安慰者。她坚定地看待生活，并以勇气和热情承担起自己的责任。她全身心投入到那些她被教导称她为叔叔和表兄弟的人身上。当她回忆起她灿烂的笑容并把它们洒在我们身上时，她从来没有像现在这样迷人。她努力让我们忘记，甚至忘记了自己的遗憾。

The day of my departure at length arrived. Clerval spent the last evening with us. He had endeavoured to persuade his father to permit him to accompany me and to become my fellow student, but in vain. His father was a narrow-minded trader and saw idleness and ruin in the aspirations and ambition of his son. Henry deeply felt the misfortune of being debarred from a liberal education. He said little, but when he spoke I read in his kindling eye and in his animated glance a restrained but firm resolve not to be chained to the miserable details of commerce.
我出发的日子终于到来了。克莱瓦尔和我们一起度过了最后一个晚上。他曾试图说服他的父亲允许他陪伴我并成为我的同学，但没有成功。他的父亲是一位心胸狭隘的商人，他在儿子的抱负和野心中看到了懒惰和毁灭。亨利深深地感受到了被禁止接受自由教育的不幸。他话不多，但当他说话时，我从他那双炽热的眼睛和他活泼的眼神中读到一种克制但坚定的决心，即不被商业的悲惨细节所束缚。

We sat late. We could not tear ourselves away from each other nor persuade ourselves to say the word ‘Farewell!’ It was said, and we retired under the pretence of seeking repose, each fancying that the other was deceived; but when at morning’s dawn I descended to the carriage which was to convey me away, they were all there—my father again to bless me, Clerval to press my hand once more, my Elizabeth to renew her entreaties that I would write often and to bestow the last feminine attentions on her playmate and friend.
我们坐得很晚。我们无法分开，也无法说服自己说出“再见”这个词！说完，我们就假装要休息，各自退了出去，彼此都以为对方受了欺骗；但我们却都以为对方被欺骗了。但是，当黎明时分，我下楼到要送我走的马车时，他们都在那里——我的父亲再次祝福我，克莱瓦尔再次握着我的手，我的伊丽莎白再次恳求我经常写信，并给我写信。将最后的女性关怀给予她的玩伴和朋友。

I threw myself into the chaise that was to convey me away and indulged in the most melancholy reflections. I, who had ever been surrounded by amiable companions, continually engaged in endeavouring to bestow mutual pleasure—I was now alone. In the university whither I was going I must form my own friends and be my own protector. My life had hitherto been remarkably secluded and domestic, and this had given me invincible repugnance to new countenances. I loved my brothers, Elizabeth, and Clerval; these were ‘old familiar faces,’ but I believed myself totally unfitted for the company of strangers. Such were my reflections as I commenced my journey; but as I proceeded, my spirits and hopes rose. I ardently desired the acquisition of knowledge. I had often, when at home, thought it hard to remain during my youth cooped up in one place and had longed to enter the world and take my station among other human beings. Now my desires were complied with, and it would, indeed, have been folly to repent.
我一头扎进准备送我离开的马车上，陷入了最忧郁的沉思。我，曾经被友善的同伴包围着，不断地努力给予彼此快乐——现在我孤身一人了。在我要去的大学里，我必须结交自己的朋友，成为自己的保护者。迄今为止，我的生活一直是非常与世隔绝的家庭生活，这使我对新面孔产生了无以复加的厌恶。我爱我的兄弟伊丽莎白和克莱瓦尔；这些都是“熟悉的老面孔”，但我相信自己完全不适合与陌生人为伍。这就是我开始旅程时的想法。但当我继续前行时，我的精神和希望也随之升起。我热切地渴望获得知识。当我在家的时候，常常觉得自己年轻时被关在一个地方是很困难的，所以渴望进入这个世界，在其他人中占据一席之地。现在我的愿望得到了满足，如果再悔改，那就太愚蠢了。

I had sufficient leisure for these and many other reflections during my journey to Ingolstadt, which was long and fatiguing. At length the high white steeple of the town met my eyes. I alighted and was conducted to my solitary apartment to spend the evening as I pleased.
在前往因戈尔施塔特的漫长而疲惫的旅程中，我有足够的空闲时间进行这些思考和许多其他思考。最后，小镇高高的白色尖塔映入我的眼帘。我下了车，被带到我单独的公寓，随心所欲地度过一个晚上。

The next morning I delivered my letters of introduction and paid a visit to some of the principal professors. Chance—or rather the evil influence, the Angel of Destruction, which asserted omnipotent sway over me from the moment I turned my reluctant steps from my father’s door—led me first to M. Krempe, professor of natural philosophy. He was an uncouth man, but deeply imbued in the secrets of his science. He asked me several questions concerning my progress in the different branches of science appertaining to natural philosophy. I replied carelessly, and partly in contempt, mentioned the names of my alchemists as the principal authors I had studied. The professor stared. ‘Have you,’ he said, ‘really spent your time in studying such nonsense?’
第二天早上我递交了介绍信并拜访了一些主要教授。机会——或者更确切地说，邪恶的影响力，毁灭天使，从我不情愿地走出父亲家门的那一刻起，它就对我施加了无所不能的影响——首先把我引向了自然哲学教授克伦佩先生。他是一个粗鲁的人，但深深地沉浸在他的科学秘密中。他问了我几个关于我在自然哲学相关科学不同分支方面的进展的问题。我漫不经心地回答，带着几分轻蔑，提到了我的炼金术士的名字，他们是我研究过的主要作者。教授凝视着。 “你真的花了时间研究这些废话吗？”他说。

I replied in the affirmative. ‘Every minute,’ continued M. Krempe with warmth, ‘every instant that you have wasted on those books is utterly and entirely lost. You have burdened your memory with exploded systems and useless names. Good God! In what desert land have you lived, where no one was kind enough to inform you that these fancies which you have so greedily imbibed are a thousand years old and as musty as they are ancient? I little expected, in this enlightened and scientific age, to find a disciple of Albertus Magnus and Paracelsus. My dear sir, you must begin your studies entirely anew.’
