我的回答是肯定的。 “每一分钟，”克伦佩先生热情地继续说道，“你在这些书上浪费的每一刻都彻底消失了。”爆炸的系统和无用的名字给你的记忆带来了负担。天哪！你生活在什么样的沙漠土地上，没有人好心地告诉你，你如此贪婪地吸收的这些幻想已经有一千多年的历史了，而且像它们古老一样发霉了？我没想到，在这个开明的科学时代，会找到阿尔伯特·马格努斯和帕拉塞尔苏斯的弟子。我亲爱的先生，您必须重新开始学习。

So saying, he stepped aside and wrote down a list of several books treating of natural philosophy which he desired me to procure, and dismissed me after mentioning that in the beginning of the following week he intended to commence a course of lectures upon natural philosophy in its general relations, and that M. Waldman, a fellow professor, would lecture upon chemistry the alternate days that he omitted.
说着，他走到一边，写下了一份清单，列出了几本他希望我购买的有关自然哲学的书籍，并在提到下周初他打算在它的一般关系，而且沃尔德曼先生，一位教授，每隔几天他就会讲化学课。

I returned home not disappointed, for I have said that I had long considered those authors useless whom the professor reprobated; but I returned not at all the more inclined to recur to these studies in any shape. M. Krempe was a little squat man with a gruff voice and a repulsive countenance; the teacher, therefore, did not prepossess me in favour of his pursuits. In rather a too philosophical and connected a strain, perhaps, I have given an account of the conclusions I had come to concerning them in my early years. As a child I had not been content with the results promised by the modern professors of natural science. With a confusion of ideas only to be accounted for by my extreme youth and my want of a guide on such matters, I had retrod the steps of knowledge along the paths of time and exchanged the discoveries of recent inquirers for the dreams of forgotten alchemists. Besides, I had a contempt for the uses of modern natural philosophy. It was very different when the masters of the science sought immortality and power; such views, although futile, were grand; but now the scene was changed. The ambition of the inquirer seemed to limit itself to the annihilation of those visions on which my interest in science was chiefly founded. I was required to exchange chimeras of boundless grandeur for realities of little worth.
我回到家并没有失望，因为我说过，我一直认为那些被教授斥责的作家毫无用处。但我回来后并没有更倾向于以任何形式重复这些研究。克伦佩先生身材矮小，身材矮胖，声音粗哑，面容令人厌恶。因此，老师并没有让我赞成他的追求。也许，我以一种过于哲学化和相关的张力，阐述了我早年就这些问题得出的结论。当我还是个孩子的时候，我对现代自然科学教授所承诺的结果并不满意。由于我年纪轻轻，思想混乱，而且我在这些问题上缺乏指导，我沿着时间的道路回顾了知识的脚步，用最近探索者的发现换取了被遗忘的炼金术士的梦想。此外，我对现代自然哲学的运用很蔑视。当科学大师寻求永生和力量时，情况就大不相同了。这些观点虽然徒劳，但却是伟大的。但现在场景变了。探究者的野心似乎仅限于消灭我对科学的兴趣主要建立在其上的那些愿景。我被要求用毫无价值的现实来交换无限宏伟的幻想。

Such were my reflections during the first two or three days of my residence at Ingolstadt, which were chiefly spent in becoming acquainted with the localities and the principal residents in my new abode. But as the ensuing week commenced, I thought of the information which M. Krempe had given me concerning the lectures. And although I could not consent to go and hear that little conceited fellow deliver sentences out of a pulpit, I recollected what he had said of M. Waldman, whom I had never seen, as he had hitherto been out of town.
这是我在因戈尔施塔特居住的头两三天的思考，主要是为了熟悉新住所的地方和主要居民。但随着接下来的一周开始，我想起了克伦佩先生给我的有关讲座的信息。虽然我不能同意去听那个自负的小家伙在讲坛上宣讲，但我记得他对沃尔德曼先生说过的话，我从未见过他，因为他迄今为止一直在外地。

Partly from curiosity and partly from idleness, I went into the lecturing room, which M. Waldman entered shortly after. This professor was very unlike his colleague. He appeared about fifty years of age, but with an aspect expressive of the greatest benevolence; a few grey hairs covered his temples, but those at the back of his head were nearly black. His person was short but remarkably erect and his voice the sweetest I had ever heard. He began his lecture by a recapitulation of the history of chemistry and the various improvements made by different men of learning, pronouncing with fervour the names of the most distinguished discoverers. He then took a cursory view of the present state of the science and explained many of its elementary terms. After having made a few preparatory experiments, he concluded with a panegyric upon modern chemistry, the terms of which I shall never forget: ‘The ancient teachers of this science,’ said he, ‘promised impossibilities and performed nothing. The modern masters promise very little; they know that metals cannot be transmuted and that the elixir of life is a chimera but these philosophers, whose hands seem only made to dabble in dirt, and their eyes to pore over the microscope or crucible, have indeed performed miracles. They penetrate into the recesses of nature and show how she works in her hiding-places. They ascend into the heavens; they have discovered how the blood circulates, and the nature of the air we breathe. They have acquired new and almost unlimited powers; they can command the thunders of heaven, mimic the earthquake, and even mock the invisible world with its own shadows.’
部分出于好奇，部分出于闲置，我走进了讲堂，不久之后瓦尔德曼先生也进入了教室。这位教授与他的同事很不一样。他看起来大约五十岁，但脸上却流露出极大的仁慈。他的太阳穴上覆盖着几根灰白的头发，但后脑勺的头发却几乎是黑色的。他身材矮小，但非常挺拔，他的声音是我听过的最甜美的。他以重述化学史和不同学者所做的各种改进开始了他的演讲，并热情地念出了最杰出的发现者的名字。然后，他粗略地了解了科学的现状，并解释了许多基本术语。在做了一些准备性实验之后，他对现代化学进行了一番颂扬，其中的术语我永远不会忘记：“这门科学的古代老师，”他说，“承诺了不可能的事情，却什么也没做。”现代大师的承诺很少；他们知道金属无法改变，长生不老药只是一种幻想，但这些哲学家，他们的双手似乎只能涉足泥土，而他们的眼睛却只能仔细观察显微镜或坩埚，他们确实创造了奇迹。它们深入大自然的深处，展示她如何在隐藏的地方工作。他们升入诸天；他们发现了血液如何循环以及我们呼吸的空气的性质。他们获得了新的、几乎无限的权力；他们可以指挥天上的雷霆，模仿地震，甚至用自己的影子嘲笑无形的世界。

Such were the professor’s words—rather let me say such the words of the fate—enounced to destroy me. As he went on I felt as if my soul were grappling with a palpable enemy; one by one the various keys were touched which formed the mechanism of my being; chord after chord was sounded, and soon my mind was filled with one thought, one conception, one purpose. So much has been done, exclaimed the soul of Frankenstein—more, far more, will I achieve; treading in the steps already marked, I will pioneer a new way, explore unknown powers, and unfold to the world the deepest mysteries of creation.
这就是教授的话——更确切地说，是命运的话——宣告要毁灭我。当他继续说下去时，我感觉自己的灵魂正在与一个明显的敌人搏斗。各种按键被一一触动，形成了我存在的机制；一个又一个的和弦响起，很快我的脑海里就充满了一个想法，一个构想，一个目的。弗兰肯斯坦的灵魂感叹道，我们已经做了很多事情——我还会取得更多、更多的成就；踏着已经标记的脚步，我将开拓一条新的道路，探索未知的力量，向世界揭开造物最深的奥秘。

I closed not my eyes that night. My internal being was in a state of insurrection and turmoil; I felt that order would thence arise, but I had no power to produce it. By degrees, after the morning’s dawn, sleep came. I awoke, and my yesternight’s thoughts were as a dream. There only remained a resolution to return to my ancient studies and to devote myself to a science for which I believed myself to possess a natural talent. On the same day I paid M. Waldman a visit. His manners in private were even more mild and attractive than in public, for there was a certain dignity in his mien during his lecture which in his own house was replaced by the greatest affability and kindness. I gave him pretty nearly the same account of my former pursuits as I had given to his fellow professor. He heard with attention the little narration concerning my studies and smiled at the names of Cornelius Agrippa and Paracelsus, but without the contempt that M. Krempe had exhibited. He said that ‘These were men to whose indefatigable zeal modern philosophers were indebted for most of the foundations of their knowledge. They had left to us, as an easier task, to give new names and arrange in connected classifications the facts which they in a great degree had been the instruments of bringing to light. The labours of men of genius, however erroneously directed, scarcely ever fail in ultimately turning to the solid advantage of mankind.’ I listened to his statement, which was delivered without any presumption or affectation, and then added that his lecture had removed my prejudices against modern chemists; I expressed myself in measured terms, with the modesty and deference due from a youth to his instructor, without letting escape (inexperience in life would have made me ashamed) any of the enthusiasm which stimulated my intended labours. I requested his advice concerning the books I ought to procure.
那天晚上我没有闭上眼睛。我的内心处于一种叛逆和混乱的状态；我觉得秩序将会出现，但我没有能力产生它。黎明之后，渐渐地，睡眠来临了。我醒了，昨天的想法就像一场梦。我只剩下一个决心，那就是回到我古老的研究，并致力于一门我相信自己拥有天赋的科学。同一天，我拜访了沃尔德曼先生。他私下里的举止甚至比公开场合更加温和和有吸引力，因为他在演讲时的举止有一定的尊严，而在他自己的家里，这种举止却被最大的和蔼可亲和友善所取代。我向他讲述了我以前的追求，几乎与我向他的教授同事讲述的一样。他专注地听着关于我的研究的小叙述，对科尼利厄斯·阿格里帕和帕拉塞尔苏斯的名字微笑，但没有克伦佩先生表现出的蔑视。他说：“现代哲学家的大部分知识基础都归功于这些人不知疲倦的热情。他们留给我们的任务是一项更容易的任务，即赋予新的名称，并将事实进行相关的分类，而这些事实在很大程度上是他们揭露的工具。天才们的劳动，无论方向多么错误，最终都不会失败，为人类带来坚实的利益。’我听了他的发言，他的发言没有任何假设或矫揉造作，然后补充说，他的演讲消除了我对现代化学家的偏见；我以年轻人对导师应有的谦虚和尊敬的态度，谨慎地表达了自己的意思，但没有放过任何激发我预期工作的热情（生活经验不足会让我感到羞愧）。我向他请教关于我应该购买的书籍的建议。

‘I am happy,’ said M. Waldman, ‘to have gained a disciple; and if your application equals your ability, I have no doubt of your success. Chemistry is that branch of natural philosophy in which the greatest improvements have been and may be made; it is on that account that I have made it my peculiar study; but at the same time, I have not neglected the other branches of science. A man would make but a very sorry chemist if he attended to that department of human knowledge alone. If your wish is to become really a man of science and not merely a petty experimentalist, I should advise you to apply to every branch of natural philosophy, including mathematics.’ He then took me into his laboratory and explained to me the uses of his various machines, instructing me as to what I ought to procure and promising me the use of his own when I should have advanced far enough in the science not to derange their mechanism. He also gave me the list of books which I had requested, and I took my leave.
“我很高兴，”沃尔德曼先生说，“获得了一个弟子；如果你的申请与你的能力相匹配，我毫不怀疑你的成功。化学是自然哲学的一个分支，其中已经并可能取得最大的进步。正因为如此，我才将它作为我的特殊研究。但与此同时，我并没有忽视其他科学分支。如果一个人只关注人类知识的那个部门，他就会成为一个非常遗憾的化学家。如果你的愿望是成为一名真正的科学家，而不仅仅是一名小实验家，我建议你应用自然哲学的每一个分支，包括数学。”然后他带我进入他的实验室，并向我解释了他的方法的用途。各种机器，指导我应该购买什么，并承诺当我在科学上已经足够先进而不会扰乱它们的机制时，我可以使用他自己的机器。他还给了我所需的书籍清单，然后我就告辞了。

Thus ended a day memorable to me; it decided my future destiny.
令我难忘的一天就这样结束了；它决定了我未来的命运。

Chapter 4
第4章

From this day natural philosophy, and particularly chemistry, in the most comprehensive sense of the term, became nearly my sole occupation. I read with ardour those works, so full of genius and discrimination, which modern inquirers have written on these subjects. I attended the lectures and cultivated the acquaintance of the men of science of the university, and I found even in M. Krempe a great deal of sound sense and real information, combined, it is true, with a repulsive physiognomy and manners, but not on that account the less valuable. In M. Waldman I found a true friend. His gentleness was never tinged by dogmatism, and his instructions were given with an air of frankness and good nature that banished every idea of pedantry. In a thousand ways he smoothed for me the path of knowledge and made the most abstruse inquiries clear and facile to my apprehension. My application was at first fluctuating and uncertain; it gained strength as I proceeded and soon became so ardent and eager that the stars often disappeared in the light of morning whilst I was yet engaged in my laboratory.
从今天起，自然哲学，尤其是最全面意义上的化学，几乎成为我唯一的职业。我满怀热情地阅读了现代探索者关于这些主题所写的那些充满天才和洞察力的作品。我参加了讲座，并结识了大学里的科学家，我什至在克伦佩先生身上发现了大量的声音感觉和真实的信息，确实，与令人厌恶的相貌和举止结合在一起，但不是因此价值较低。在沃尔德曼先生身上，我找到了一位真正的朋友。他的温和从来没有教条主义的色彩，他的指示是带着坦率和善良的神情，消除了一切迂腐的想法。他以一千种方式为我铺平了知识之路，使最深奥的探究变得清晰易懂。我的申请一开始是波动且不确定的；当我继续前进时，它变得越来越强大，很快就变得如此热情和渴望，以至于当我还在实验室工作时，星星常常消失在晨光中。

As I applied so closely, it may be easily conceived that my progress was rapid. My ardour was indeed the astonishment of the students, and my proficiency that of the masters. Professor Krempe often asked me, with a sly smile, how Cornelius Agrippa went on, whilst M. Waldman expressed the most heartfelt exultation in my progress. Two years passed in this manner, during which I paid no visit to Geneva, but was engaged, heart and soul, in the pursuit of some discoveries which I hoped to make. None but those who have experienced them can conceive of the enticements of science. In other studies you go as far as others have gone before you, and there is nothing more to know; but in a scientific pursuit there is continual food for discovery and wonder. A mind of moderate capacity which closely pursues one study must infallibly arrive at great proficiency in that study; and I, who continually sought the attainment of one object of pursuit and was solely wrapped up in this, improved so rapidly that at the end of two years I made some discoveries in the improvement of some chemical instruments, which procured me great esteem and admiration at the university. When I had arrived at this point and had become as well acquainted with the theory and practice of natural philosophy as depended on the lessons of any of the professors at Ingolstadt, my residence there being no longer conducive to my improvements, I thought of returning to my friends and my native town, when an incident happened that protracted my stay.
由于我如此认真地申请，所以很容易想象我的进步是很快的。我的热情确实让学生们惊叹，我的熟练程度确实让老师们惊叹。克伦佩教授经常带着狡猾的微笑问我科尼利厄斯·阿格里帕进展得怎么样，而瓦尔德曼先生则对我的进步表示由衷的欣喜。两年就这样过去了，期间我没有去日内瓦，而是全心全意地追求我希望取得的一些发现。除了那些经历过的人之外，没有人能够想象科学的诱惑。在其他的研究中，你就已经达到了别人在你之前已经达到的程度，并且没有什么可知道的了；但在科学追求中，不断有发现和奇迹的源泉。一个中等能力的人，如果认真钻研一门学科，一定会在这门学科上达到非常熟练的程度。而我，不断地追求一个目标，一心一意地追求这一目标，进步如此之快，两年后，我在一些化学仪器的改进上有了一些发现，这让我非常尊重和钦佩。在大学里。当我到达这一点，并且已经像因戈尔施塔特任何一位教授的课程一样熟悉自然哲学的理论和实践时，我在那里的住所不再有利于我的进步，我想回到我的朋友和我的家乡发生了一起事件，导致我的逗留时间延长了。

One of the phenomena which had peculiarly attracted my attention was the structure of the human frame, and, indeed, any animal endued with life. Whence, I often asked myself, did the principle of life proceed? It was a bold question, and one which has ever been considered as a mystery; yet with how many things are we upon the brink of becoming acquainted, if cowardice or carelessness did not restrain our inquiries. I revolved these circumstances in my mind and determined thenceforth to apply myself more particularly to those branches of natural philosophy which relate to physiology. Unless I had been animated by an almost supernatural enthusiasm, my application to this study would have been irksome and almost intolerable. To examine the causes of life, we must first have recourse to death. I became acquainted with the science of anatomy, but this was not sufficient; I must also observe the natural decay and corruption of the human body. In my education my father had taken the greatest precautions that my mind should be impressed with no supernatural horrors. I do not ever remember to have trembled at a tale of superstition or to have feared the apparition of a spirit. Darkness had no effect upon my fancy, and a churchyard was to me merely the receptacle of bodies deprived of life, which, from being the seat of beauty and strength, had become food for the worm. Now I was led to examine the cause and progress of this decay and forced to spend days and nights in vaults and charnel-houses. My attention was fixed upon every object the most insupportable to the delicacy of the human feelings. I saw how the fine form of man was degraded and wasted; I beheld the corruption of death succeed to the blooming cheek of life; I saw how the worm inherited the wonders of the eye and brain. I paused, examining and analysing all the minutiae of causation, as exemplified in the change from life to death, and death to life, until from the midst of this darkness a sudden light broke in upon me—a light so brilliant and wondrous, yet so simple, that while I became dizzy with the immensity of the prospect which it illustrated, I was surprised that among so many men of genius who had directed their inquiries towards the same science, that I alone should be reserved to discover so astonishing a secret.
特别引起我注意的现象之一是人体的结构，事实上，任何动物都具有生命。我时常问自己，生命的法则从何而来？这是一个大胆的问题，也一直被认为是一个谜。然而，如果怯懦或粗心没有限制我们的探究，我们还有多少事情即将熟悉。我在脑海中思考了这些情况，并决定从那时起我将更加特别地致力于那些与生理​​学相关的自然哲学分支。除非我被近乎超自然的热情所激励，否则我对这项研究的申请将会令人厌烦，几乎无法忍受。要考察生命的原因，必须首先求助于死亡。我开始熟悉解剖学，但这还不够。我还必须观察人体的自然腐烂和腐败。在我的教育中，父亲采取了最大的预防措施，不让我的脑海中留下任何超自然的恐怖。我不记得曾因迷信故事而颤抖过，或害怕过幽灵的出现。黑暗对我的幻想没有影响，教堂墓地对我来说只是被剥夺生命的尸体的容器，它们不再是美丽和力量的所在地，而是成为蠕虫的食物。现在我被引导去检查这种腐烂的原因和进展，并被迫在金库和停尸房里度过日日夜夜。我的注意力集中在每一个最难以忍受人类情感脆弱的物体上。 我看到人类的美好形态是如何被退化和浪费的；我看到死亡的腐化接替了生命绽放的脸颊；我看到了蠕虫如何继承了眼睛和大脑的奇迹。我停下来，检查和分析因果关系的所有细枝末节，例如从生到死，从死到生的变化，直到在这黑暗之中，一道光突然照到了我身上——那光是如此灿烂和奇妙，但如此简单，以至于当我对它所描绘的广阔前景感到头晕目眩时，我感到惊讶的是，在这么多将他们的研究引向同一门科学的天才中，只有我一个人竟然有能力发现如此惊人的秘密。

Remember, I am not recording the vision of a madman. The sun does not more certainly shine in the heavens than that which I now affirm is true. Some miracle might have produced it, yet the stages of the discovery were distinct and probable. After days and nights of incredible labour and fatigue, I succeeded in discovering the cause of generation and life; nay, more, I became myself capable of bestowing animation upon lifeless matter.
请记住，我并不是在记录一个疯子的幻象。太阳在天空中的照耀并不比我现在所确认的更确定。它可能是某种奇迹产生的，但发现的阶段是明确且可能的。经过日日夜夜的令人难以置信的劳动和疲劳，我成功地找到了生成和生命的原因；不仅如此，我还变得能够赋予无生命的物质以活力。

The astonishment which I had at first experienced on this discovery soon gave place to delight and rapture. After so much time spent in painful labour, to arrive at once at the summit of my desires was the most gratifying consummation of my toils. But this discovery was so great and overwhelming that all the steps by which I had been progressively led to it were obliterated, and I beheld only the result. What had been the study and desire of the wisest men since the creation of the world was now within my grasp. Not that, like a magic scene, it all opened upon me at once: the information I had obtained was of a nature rather to direct my endeavours so soon as I should point them towards the object of my search than to exhibit that object already accomplished. I was like the Arabian who had been buried with the dead and found a passage to life, aided only by one glimmering and seemingly ineffectual light.
我最初对这一发现感到惊讶，很快就变成了喜悦和狂喜。在经历了这么多时间的痛苦劳动之后，立即达到我的愿望的顶峰是我辛劳中最令人欣慰的完成。但这个发现是如此伟大和压倒性，以至于我逐步引导到它的所有步骤都被抹去了，我只看到了结果。自创世以来最智者的研究和愿望现在都在我的掌握之中。并不是说，就像一个神奇的场景，一切都立即向我展开：我所获得的信息本质上是为了指导我的努力，以便我将它们指向我的搜索对象，而不是展示已经完成的目标。我就像一个与死者一起埋葬的阿拉伯人，只靠一束微弱的、看似无效的光的帮助，找到了一条通往生命的通道。

I see by your eagerness and the wonder and hope which your eyes express, my friend, that you expect to be informed of the secret with which I am acquainted; that cannot be; listen patiently until the end of my story, and you will easily perceive why I am reserved upon that subject. I will not lead you on, unguarded and ardent as I then was, to your destruction and infallible misery. Learn from me, if not by my precepts, at least by my example, how dangerous is the acquirement of knowledge and how much happier that man is who believes his native town to be the world, than he who aspires to become greater than his nature will allow.
我的朋友，从你的热切以及你眼中所流露出的惊奇和希望中，我看出你期望被告知我所知道的秘密。那不可能；耐心地听完我的故事，你就会很容易理解为什么我在这个问题上持保留态度。我不会像当时那样毫无防备、热心地带领你们走向毁灭和绝对的痛苦。向我学习，即使不是通过我的戒律，至少通过我的榜样，获取知识是多么危险，相信自己的家乡就是世界的人比那些渴望变得比他的本性更伟大的人要快乐得多会允许。

When I found so astonishing a power placed within my hands, I hesitated a long time concerning the manner in which I should employ it. Although I possessed the capacity of bestowing animation, yet to prepare a frame for the reception of it, with all its intricacies of fibres, muscles, and veins, still remained a work of inconceivable difficulty and labour. I doubted at first whether I should attempt the creation of a being like myself, or one of simpler organization; but my imagination was too much exalted by my first success to permit me to doubt of my ability to give life to an animal as complete and wonderful as man. The materials at present within my command hardly appeared adequate to so arduous an undertaking, but I doubted not that I should ultimately succeed. I prepared myself for a multitude of reverses; my operations might be incessantly baffled, and at last my work be imperfect, yet when I considered the improvement which every day takes place in science and mechanics, I was encouraged to hope my present attempts would at least lay the foundations of future success. Nor could I consider the magnitude and complexity of my plan as any argument of its impracticability. It was with these feelings that I began the creation of a human being. As the minuteness of the parts formed a great hindrance to my speed, I resolved, contrary to my first intention, to make the being of a gigantic stature, that is to say, about eight feet in height, and proportionably large. After having formed this determination and having spent some months in successfully collecting and arranging my materials, I began.
当我发现自己手中掌握着如此惊人的力量时，我犹豫了很长一段时间，不知道该如何运用它。尽管我拥有赋予动画的能力，但准备一个接受它的框架，以及它复杂的纤维、肌肉和静脉，仍然是一项难以想象的困难和劳动。一开始我怀疑是否应该尝试创造一个像我一样的存在，或者一个更简单的组织；但我的想象力因我的第一次成功而变得过于丰富，以至于我无法怀疑自己是否有能力赋予动物像人类一样完整和美妙的生命。目前我掌握的材料似乎不足以完成如此​​艰巨的任务，但我毫不怀疑我最终会成功。我做好了面对许多挫折的准备；我的操作可能会不断地受挫，最终我的工作也不完美，但当我想到科学和机械领域每天都在进步时，我受到鼓舞，希望我目前的尝试至少能为未来的成功奠定基础。我也不能将我的计划的规模和复杂性视为其不切实际的理由。正是带着这些感觉，我开始创造一个人。由于这些部件的微小对我的速度构成了很大的障碍，所以与我的最初意图相反，我决定将这个物体做成一个巨大的身材，也就是说，大约八英尺高，并且比例很大。在下了这个决心并花了几个月的时间成功收集和整理我的材料后，我开始了。

No one can conceive the variety of feelings which bore me onwards, like a hurricane, in the first enthusiasm of success. Life and death appeared to me ideal bounds, which I should first break through, and pour a torrent of light into our dark world. A new species would bless me as its creator and source; many happy and excellent natures would owe their being to me. No father could claim the gratitude of his child so completely as I should deserve theirs. Pursuing these reflections, I thought that if I could bestow animation upon lifeless matter, I might in process of time (although I now found it impossible) renew life where death had apparently devoted the body to corruption.
没有人能够想象，在第一次成功的热情中，我所感受到的各种感受，就像飓风一样。生与死对我来说似乎是理想的界限，我应该首先突破它，为我们黑暗的世界注入一股光明。一个新物种将祝福我作为它的创造者和源头；许多快乐而优秀的人的存在都归功于我。没有哪个父亲能够像我一样完全地得到孩子的感激。追寻这些思考，我想，如果我能够赋予无生命的物质以活力，我可能会在时间的过程中（尽管我现在发现这是不可能的）在死亡显然使身体腐烂的地方恢复生命。

These thoughts supported my spirits, while I pursued my undertaking with unremitting ardour. My cheek had grown pale with study, and my person had become emaciated with confinement. Sometimes, on the very brink of certainty, I failed; yet still I clung to the hope which the next day or the next hour might realize. One secret which I alone possessed was the hope to which I had dedicated myself; and the moon gazed on my midnight labours, while, with unrelaxed and breathless eagerness, I pursued nature to her hiding-places. Who shall conceive the horrors of my secret toil as I dabbled among the unhallowed damps of the grave or tortured the living animal to animate the lifeless clay? My limbs now tremble, and my eyes swim with the remembrance; but then a resistless and almost frantic impulse urged me forward; I seemed to have lost all soul or sensation but for this one pursuit. It was indeed but a passing trance, that only made me feel with renewed acuteness so soon as, the unnatural stimulus ceasing to operate, I had returned to my old habits. I collected bones from charnel-houses and disturbed, with profane fingers, the tremendous secrets of the human frame. In a solitary chamber, or rather cell, at the top of the house, and separated from all the other apartments by a gallery and staircase, I kept my workshop of filthy creation; my eyeballs were starting from their sockets in attending to the details of my employment. The dissecting room and the slaughter-house furnished many of my materials; and often did my human nature turn with loathing from my occupation, whilst, still urged on by an eagerness which perpetually increased, I brought my work near to a conclusion.
这些想法支撑着我的精神，让我以不懈的热情去追求自己的事业。我的脸因学习而变得苍白，我的人因禁闭而变得憔悴。有时，就在确定性的边缘，我却失败了；但我仍然抱有第二天或下一小时可能实现的希望。我独自拥有的一个秘密就是我为之献身的希望。月亮凝视着我午夜的劳作，而我则以不放松、气喘吁吁的渴望，追寻着大自然的藏身之处。当我在坟墓里肮脏的湿气中涉足，或者折磨活生生的动物以使无生命的泥土复活时，谁能想象我秘密辛劳的恐怖？我的四肢现在在颤抖，我的眼睛因回忆而游动；但随后一种无法抗拒的、近乎疯狂的冲动催促着我向前走。除了这一追求，我似乎失去了所有的灵魂和感觉。这确实只是短暂的恍惚，只有当不自然的刺激停止发挥作用，我又恢复了原来的习惯时，才让我感觉到新的敏锐。我从停尸房收集骨头，用亵渎的手指扰乱人体的巨大秘密。在房子顶部的一个单独的房间，或者更确切地说是牢房里，通过画廊和楼梯与所有其他公寓隔开，我保存了我的肮脏创作的工作室；我的眼球都从眼窝里跳出来，关注着我工作的细节。解剖室和屠宰场提供了我的许多材料；我的人性常常因对我的职业感到厌恶而转变，同时，在不断增长的渴望的推动下，我使我的工作接近结束。

The summer months passed while I was thus engaged, heart and soul, in one pursuit. It was a most beautiful season; never did the fields bestow a more plentiful harvest or the vines yield a more luxuriant vintage, but my eyes were insensible to the charms of nature. And the same feelings which made me neglect the scenes around me caused me also to forget those friends who were so many miles absent, and whom I had not seen for so long a time. I knew my silence disquieted them, and I well remembered the words of my father: ‘I know that while you are pleased with yourself you will think of us with affection, and we shall hear regularly from you. You must pardon me if I regard any interruption in your correspondence as a proof that your other duties are equally neglected.’
暑假的几个月过去了，我就这样全身心地投入到一项追求中。那是一个最美的季节；田野从来没有如此丰收，葡萄树从来没有如此丰沛，但我的眼睛却对大自然的魅力麻木不仁。同样的感觉让我忽视了周围的景色，也让我忘记了那些远隔千里、许久未见的朋友。我知道我的沉默让他们感到不安，我清楚地记得父亲的话：“我知道，当你对自己感到满意时，你会充满感情地想到我们，我们会定期收到你的消息。”如果我认为你的通信中的任何中断都证明你的其他职责同样被忽视，你必须原谅我。

I knew well therefore what would be my father’s feelings, but I could not tear my thoughts from my employment, loathsome in itself, but which had taken an irresistible hold of my imagination. I wished, as it were, to procrastinate all that related to my feelings of affection until the great object, which swallowed up every habit of my nature, should be completed.
因此，我很清楚父亲的感受是什么，但我无法将自己的想法从我的工作中抽离出来，它本身令人厌​​恶，但却不可抗拒地占据了我的想象力。可以说，我希望推迟所有与我的感情有关的事情，直到完成这个伟大的目标，这个目标吞噬了我本性的每一个习惯。

I then thought that my father would be unjust if he ascribed my neglect to vice or faultiness on my part, but I am now convinced that he was justified in conceiving that I should not be altogether free from blame. A human being in perfection ought always to preserve a calm and peaceful mind and never to allow passion or a transitory desire to disturb his tranquillity. I do not think that the pursuit of knowledge is an exception to this rule. If the study to which you apply yourself has a tendency to weaken your affections and to destroy your taste for those simple pleasures in which no alloy can possibly mix, then that study is certainly unlawful, that is to say, not befitting the human mind. If this rule were always observed; if no man allowed any pursuit whatsoever to interfere with the tranquillity of his domestic affections, Greece had not been enslaved, Caesar would have spared his country, America would have been discovered more gradually, and the empires of Mexico and Peru had not been destroyed.
当时我想，如果我的父亲将我的疏忽归咎于我的恶习或过错，那他就是不公正的，但现在我确信，他认为我不应该完全免受责备是有道理的。一个完美的人应该始终保持一颗平静祥和的心，决不让激情或短暂的欲望扰乱他的平静。我不认为对知识的追求是这条规则的例外。如果你自己从事的研究有削弱你的感情并破坏你对那些不可能混合的简单快乐的品味的倾向，那么这种研究肯定是非法的，也就是说，不适合人类的思想。如果始终遵守这条规则；如果没有人允许任何追求干扰他家庭感情的平静，希腊就不会被奴役，凯撒就会饶恕他的国家，美洲就会逐渐被发现，墨西哥和秘鲁帝国就不会被摧毁。

But I forget that I am moralizing in the most interesting part of my tale, and your looks remind me to proceed. My father made no reproach in his letters and only took notice of my science by inquiring into my occupations more particularly than before. Winter, spring, and summer passed away during my labours; but I did not watch the blossom or the expanding leaves—sights which before always yielded me supreme delight—so deeply was I engrossed in my occupation. The leaves of that year had withered before my work drew near to a close, and now every day showed me more plainly how well I had succeeded. But my enthusiasm was checked by my anxiety, and I appeared rather like one doomed by slavery to toil in the mines, or any other unwholesome trade than an artist occupied by his favourite employment. Every night I was oppressed by a slow fever, and I became nervous to a most painful degree; the fall of a leaf startled me, and I shunned my fellow creatures as if I had been guilty of a crime. Sometimes I grew alarmed at the wreck I perceived that I had become; the energy of my purpose alone sustained me: my labours would soon end, and I believed that exercise and amusement would then drive away incipient disease; and I promised myself both of these when my creation should be complete.
但我忘记了我在故事中最有趣的部分中进行说教，而你的表情提醒我继续前进。我父亲在信中并没有责备我，只是通过比以前更具体地询问我的职业来注意到我的科学。冬天、春天、夏天都在我的劳动中过去了；但我并没有如此全神贯注于我的工作，而是观看花朵或展开的叶子——以前总是给我带来至高无上的喜悦的景象。那一年的树叶在我的工作接近结束之前就已经枯萎了，现在每一天都更清楚地向我展示我的成功程度。但我的热情被我的焦虑所抑制，我看起来更像是一个注定要在矿井中劳作的奴隶，或者任何其他不健康的行业，而不是一个从事他最喜欢的工作的艺术家。每天晚上，我都被缓慢的发烧所困扰，我变得紧张到最痛苦的程度。一片树叶的落下让我大吃一惊，我避开了我的同类，就好像我犯了罪一样。有时我会因为自己意识到自己已经沦为废墟而感到惊慌。我的目标的能量支撑着我：我的劳动很快就会结束，我相信锻炼和娱乐就会驱走初生的疾病；当我的创作完成时，我向自己保证了这两个目标。

Chapter 5
第5章

It was on a dreary night of November that I beheld the accomplishment of my toils. With an anxiety that almost amounted to agony, I collected the instruments of life around me, that I might infuse a spark of being into the lifeless thing that lay at my feet. It was already one in the morning; the rain pattered dismally against the panes, and my candle was nearly burnt out, when, by the glimmer of the half-extinguished light, I saw the dull yellow eye of the creature open; it breathed hard, and a convulsive motion agitated its limbs.
在十一月的一个沉闷的夜晚，我看到了我的辛劳的成果。怀着一种近乎痛苦的焦虑，我收集了周围的生命工具，以便将存在的火花注入到我脚下毫无生气的东西中。已经是凌晨一点了。雨水凄惨地拍打着窗玻璃，我的蜡烛几乎快要燃尽了，这时，借着半灭的微光，我看到那生物睁开着暗黄色的眼睛。它呼吸困难，四肢痉挛。

How can I describe my emotions at this catastrophe, or how delineate the wretch whom with such infinite pains and care I had endeavoured to form? His limbs were in proportion, and I had selected his features as beautiful. Beautiful! Great God! His yellow skin scarcely covered the work of muscles and arteries beneath; his hair was of a lustrous black, and flowing; his teeth of a pearly whiteness; but these luxuriances only formed a more horrid contrast with his watery eyes, that seemed almost of the same colour as the dun-white sockets in which they were set, his shrivelled complexion and straight black lips.
我该如何描述我在这场灾难中的情绪，或者如何描述我用如此无限的痛苦和关怀努力塑造的不幸者？他的四肢比例匀称，我选他的五官很漂亮。美丽的！大神啊！他的黄色皮肤几乎覆盖不了下面的肌肉和动脉。他的头发乌黑有光泽，飘逸。他的牙齿洁白如珍珠；但这些华丽的光彩只是与他水汪汪的眼睛形成了更可怕的对比，那双眼睛的颜色几乎与它们所在的暗褐色眼窝、干瘪的肤色和笔直的黑色嘴唇形成了更可怕的对比。

The different accidents of life are not so changeable as the feelings of human nature. I had worked hard for nearly two years, for the sole purpose of infusing life into an inanimate body. For this I had deprived myself of rest and health. I had desired it with an ardour that far exceeded moderation; but now that I had finished, the beauty of the dream vanished, and breathless horror and disgust filled my heart. Unable to endure the aspect of the being I had created, I rushed out of the room and continued a long time traversing my bed-chamber, unable to compose my mind to sleep. At length lassitude succeeded to the tumult I had before endured, and I threw myself on the bed in my clothes, endeavouring to seek a few moments of forgetfulness. But it was in vain; I slept, indeed, but I was disturbed by the wildest dreams. I thought I saw Elizabeth, in the bloom of health, walking in the streets of Ingolstadt. Delighted and surprised, I embraced her, but as I imprinted the first kiss on her lips, they became livid with the hue of death; her features appeared to change, and I thought that I held the corpse of my dead mother in my arms; a shroud enveloped her form, and I saw the grave-worms crawling in the folds of the flannel. I started from my sleep with horror; a cold dew covered my forehead, my teeth chattered, and every limb became convulsed; when, by the dim and yellow light of the moon, as it forced its way through the window shutters, I beheld the wretch— the miserable monster whom I had created. He held up the curtain of the bed; and his eyes, if eyes they may be called, were fixed on me. His jaws opened, and he muttered some inarticulate sounds, while a grin wrinkled his cheeks. He might have spoken, but I did not hear; one hand was stretched out, seemingly to detain me, but I escaped and rushed downstairs. I took refuge in the courtyard belonging to the house which I inhabited, where I remained during the rest of the night, walking up and down in the greatest agitation, listening attentively, catching and fearing each sound as if it were to announce the approach of the demoniacal corpse to which I had so miserably given life.
人生的不同意外并不像人性的感情那样变幻莫测。我辛苦工作了近两年，唯一的目的就是为无生命的身体注入生命。为此我剥夺了自己的休息和健康。我对它的渴望远远超过了节制。但现在我已经完成了，梦的美丽消失了，我的心充满了令人窒息的恐惧和厌恶。我无法忍受自己所创造的存在的样子，冲出了房间，在我的卧室里走了很长一段时间，无法安心入睡。最后，我先前所忍受的骚动取代了疲倦，我穿着衣服倒在床上，试图寻求片刻的忘却。但这是徒劳的；我确实睡着了，但我却被最疯狂的梦所打扰。我想我看到了伊丽莎白，她正健康地走在因戈尔施塔特的街道上。我既高兴又惊讶地拥抱了她，但当我将初吻印在她的嘴唇上时，她的嘴唇变得苍白，呈现出死亡的色调；她的面容似乎发生了变化，我以为我怀里抱着的是我死去母亲的尸体；裹尸布包裹着她的身体，我看到坟墓里的蠕虫在法兰绒的褶皱里爬行。我惊恐地从睡梦中惊醒。冰冷的露珠沾满了我的额头，我的牙齿打战，四肢抽搐。当月光强行穿过百叶窗的时候，借着昏黄的月光，我看到了这个不幸的人——我创造的可怜的怪物。他拉起床帘；他的眼睛，如果可以称之为眼睛的话，一直盯着我。他张开下巴，嘴里咕哝着一些含糊不清的声音，脸上挂着笑容。 他可能说话了，但我没有听见；一只手伸出来，似乎要扣住我，但我逃脱了，冲下楼。我躲在我居住的房子的院子里，整个晚上我都待在那里，焦躁不安地走来走去，聚精会神地听着，捕捉着每一个声音，并害怕它，仿佛它在宣告着我的到来。我悲惨地赋予了这具恶魔般的尸体以生命。

Oh! No mortal could support the horror of that countenance. A mummy again endued with animation could not be so hideous as that wretch. I had gazed on him while unfinished; he was ugly then, but when those muscles and joints were rendered capable of motion, it became a thing such as even Dante could not have conceived.
哦！没有凡人能够忍受那张脸的恐怖。一具再次充满活力的木乃伊不可能像那个可怜虫那么丑陋。我在未完成的时候凝视着他；那时的他很丑陋，但当那些肌肉和关节变得可以运动时，就变成了连但丁都无法想象的事情。

I passed the night wretchedly. Sometimes my pulse beat so quickly and hardly that I felt the palpitation of every artery; at others, I nearly sank to the ground through languor and extreme weakness. Mingled with this horror, I felt the bitterness of disappointment; dreams that had been my food and pleasant rest for so long a space were now become a hell to me; and the change was so rapid, the overthrow so complete!
我悲惨地度过了这一夜。有时我的脉搏跳得又快又轻，我能感觉到每条动脉的跳动；有时，我因无精打采和极度虚弱而差点倒在地上。夹杂在这种恐惧之中，我感到失望的苦涩。长期以来，梦想一直是我的食物和愉快的休息，现在对我来说变成了地狱。而且变化如此迅速，颠覆如此彻底！

Morning, dismal and wet, at length dawned and discovered to my sleepless and aching eyes the church of Ingolstadt, its white steeple and clock, which indicated the sixth hour. The porter opened the gates of the court, which had that night been my asylum, and I issued into the streets, pacing them with quick steps, as if I sought to avoid the wretch whom I feared every turning of the street would present to my view. I did not dare return to the apartment which I inhabited, but felt impelled to hurry on, although drenched by the rain which poured from a black and comfortless sky.
早晨，阴沉而潮湿，终于天亮了，在我失眠而疼痛的眼睛里发现了因戈尔施塔特教堂，它的白色尖塔和时钟，指示着第六点。门房打开了那天晚上我的避难所的法庭大门，我走进街道，快步走来走去，仿佛我试图避开那个不幸的人，我担心街道的每个转弯都会出现在我的面前。看法。我不敢回到我所居住的公寓，但觉得必须快点走，尽管被从黑暗而令人不舒服的天空倾泻而下的雨淋湿了。

I continued walking in this manner for some time, endeavouring by bodily exercise to ease the load that weighed upon my mind. I traversed the streets without any clear conception of where I was or what I was doing. My heart palpitated in the sickness of fear, and I hurried on with irregular steps, not daring to look about me:
我就这样走了一段时间，努力通过锻炼身体来减轻心里的负担。我穿过街道，对自己在哪里或在做什么没有任何清晰的概念。我的心因恐惧而狂跳，脚步不稳地快步走着，不敢回头看：

Like one who, on a lonely road,
就像一个人走在孤独的路上，

Doth walk in fear and dread,
行走在恐惧和恐惧中，

And, having once turned round, walks on,
然后，转身继续​​走，

And turns no more his head;
不再转过头；

Because he knows a frightful fiend
因为他认识一个可怕的恶魔

Doth close behind him tread.
紧紧跟在他身后。

[Coleridge’s ‘Ancient Mariner.’]
[柯勒律治的《古代水手》。]

Continuing thus, I came at length opposite to the inn at which the various diligences and carriages usually stopped. Here I paused, I knew not why; but I remained some minutes with my eyes fixed on a coach that was coming towards me from the other end of the street. As it drew nearer I observed that it was the Swiss diligence; it stopped just where I was standing, and on the door being opened, I perceived Henry Clerval, who, on seeing me, instantly sprung out. ‘My dear Frankenstein,’ exclaimed he, ‘how glad I am to see you! How fortunate that you should be here at the very moment of my alighting!’
就这样继续走下去，我终于来到了客栈对面，各种客车和马车通常都停在那里。说到这里我停了下来，我不知道为什么；但我又呆了几分钟，眼睛盯着一辆从街道另一端向我驶来的马车。当它越来越近时，我发现这是瑞士人的勤奋。它就停在我站的地方，门一打开，我就看到了亨利·克莱瓦尔，他一看到我，立刻跳了出来。 “我亲爱的弗兰肯斯坦，”他喊道，“见到你我多么高兴！多么幸运，我下车的那一刻你就在这里！”

Nothing could equal my delight on seeing Clerval; his presence brought back to my thoughts my father, Elizabeth, and all those scenes of home so dear to my recollection. I grasped his hand, and in a moment forgot my horror and misfortune; I felt suddenly, and for the first time during many months, calm and serene joy. I welcomed my friend, therefore, in the most cordial manner, and we walked towards my college. Clerval continued talking for some time about our mutual friends and his own good fortune in being permitted to come to Ingolstadt. ‘You may easily believe,’ said he, ‘how great was the difficulty to persuade my father that all necessary knowledge was not comprised in the noble art of bookkeeping; and, indeed, I believe I left him incredulous to the last, for his constant answer to my unwearied entreaties was the same as that of the Dutch schoolmaster in *The Vicar of Wakefield*: ‘I have ten thousand florins a year without Greek, I eat heartily without Greek.’ But his affection for me at length overcame his dislike of learning, and he has permitted me to undertake a voyage of discovery to the land of knowledge.’
没有什么比见到克莱瓦尔更让我高兴的了。他的出现让我想起了我的父亲伊丽莎白，以及我记忆中如此珍贵的所有家乡场景。我握住他的手，瞬间忘记了我的恐惧和不幸。我突然感到平静和安宁的喜悦，这是几个月以来的第一次。因此，我以最诚挚的方式欢迎了我的朋友，然后我们就向我的大学走去。克莱瓦尔继续谈论了我们共同的朋友和他自己被允许来到因戈尔施塔特的幸运。 “你可能很容易相信，”他说，“要说服我父亲相信高贵的簿记艺术并不包含所有必要的知识，这是多么困难；事实上，我相信我直到最后都让他难以置信，因为他对我孜孜不倦的恳求的不断回答与《韦克菲尔德牧师》中荷兰校长的回答相同：“我每年有一万弗罗林，没有希腊语， “没有希腊语，我吃得很饱。”但他对我的感情最终克服了他对学习的厌恶，他允许我踏上前往知识之地的发现之旅。

‘It gives me the greatest delight to see you; but tell me how you left my father, brothers, and Elizabeth.’
“见到你让我感到非常高兴；但告诉我你是如何离开我的父亲、兄弟和伊丽莎白的。

‘Very well, and very happy, only a little uneasy that they hear from you so seldom. By the by, I mean to lecture you a little upon their account myself. But, my dear Frankenstein,’ continued he, stopping short and gazing full in my face, ‘I did not before remark how very ill you appear; so thin and pale; you look as if you had been watching for several nights.’
“很好，也很高兴，只是有点不安，因为他们很少收到你的消息。顺便说一句，我想亲自就他们的问题向你们讲授一些知识。但是，我亲爱的弗兰肯斯坦，”他突然停下来，凝视着我的脸，继续说道，“我之前并没有注意到你看起来病得很严重；如此瘦弱、苍白；你看起来好像已经看了好几个晚上了。”

‘You have guessed right; I have lately been so deeply engaged in one occupation that I have not allowed myself sufficient rest, as you see; but I hope, I sincerely hope, that all these employments are now at an end and that I am at length free.’
‘你猜对了；正如你所看到的，我最近一直专注于一项职业，以至于没有让自己得到足够的休息。但我希望，我真诚地希望，所有这些工作现在都结束了，我终于自由了。”

I trembled excessively; I could not endure to think of, and far less to allude to, the occurrences of the preceding night. I walked with a quick pace, and we soon arrived at my college. I then reflected, and the thought made me shiver, that the creature whom I had left in my apartment might still be there, alive and walking about. I dreaded to behold this monster, but I feared still more that Henry should see him. Entreating him, therefore, to remain a few minutes at the bottom of the stairs, I darted up towards my own room. My hand was already on the lock of the door before I recollected myself. I then paused, and a cold shivering came over me. I threw the door forcibly open, as children are accustomed to do when they expect a spectre to stand in waiting for them on the other side; but nothing appeared. I stepped fearfully in: the apartment was empty, and my bedroom was also freed from its hideous guest. I could hardly believe that so great a good fortune could have befallen me, but when I became assured that my enemy had indeed fled, I clapped my hands for joy and ran down to Clerval.
我颤抖得厉害；我无法忍受想起前一天晚上发生的事情，更不用说提及了。我快步走着，很快就到了我的大学。然后我想到了，这个想法让我不寒而栗，我留在公寓里的那个生物可能还在那里，还活着，还在走来走去。我害怕看到这个怪物，但我更担心亨利会看到他。因此，我恳求他在楼梯底部停留几分钟，然后冲向自己的房间。等我回过神来时，我的手已经放在了门锁上。然后我停了下来，我浑身发冷。我用力把门打开，就像孩子们习惯做的那样，当他们期待有一个幽灵在另一边等着他们时；但什么也没有出现。我恐惧地走进去：公寓里空无一人，我的卧室里也没有那个可怕的客人。我几乎不敢相信如此巨大的好运会降临到我身上，但是当我确信我的敌人确实逃跑了时，我高兴地拍着手，跑到克莱瓦尔那里。

We ascended into my room, and the servant presently brought breakfast; but I was unable to contain myself. It was not joy only that possessed me; I felt my flesh tingle with excess of sensitiveness, and my pulse beat rapidly. I was unable to remain for a single instant in the same place; I jumped over the chairs, clapped my hands, and laughed aloud. Clerval at first attributed my unusual spirits to joy on his arrival, but when he observed me more attentively, he saw a wildness in my eyes for which he could not account, and my loud, unrestrained, heartless laughter frightened and astonished him.
我们登上房间，仆人立即送来了早餐。但我无法控制自己。令我着迷的不仅仅是喜悦；还有。我感到自己的肉因过于敏感而刺痛，脉搏跳动得很快。我无法在同一个地方停留片刻。我跳过椅子，拍着手，放声大笑。克莱瓦尔起初把我异常的精神归因于他到来时的喜悦，但当他更仔细地观察我时，他在我的眼睛里看到了一种他无法解释的狂野，而我响亮、无拘无束、无情的笑声让他感到害怕和惊讶。

‘My dear Victor,’ cried he, ‘what, for God’s sake, is the matter? Do not laugh in that manner. How ill you are! What is the cause of all this?’
“我亲爱的维克多，”他喊道，“看在上帝的份上，这是怎么回事？不要以那种方式笑。你病得多严重啊！这一切的原因是什么？

‘Do not ask me,’ cried I, putting my hands before my eyes, for I thought I saw the dreaded spectre glide into the room; ‘*he* can tell. Oh, save me! Save me!’ I imagined that the monster seized me; I struggled furiously and fell down in a fit.
“别问我，”我喊道，把手放在眼前，因为我以为我看到了可怕的幽灵溜进了房间。 ‘*他*能看出来。噢，救救我吧！救救我！”我想象着怪物抓住了我；我拼命挣扎，摔倒在地。

Poor Clerval! What must have been his feelings? A meeting, which he anticipated with such joy, so strangely turned to bitterness. But I was not the witness of his grief, for I was lifeless and did not recover my senses for a long, long time.
可怜的克莱瓦尔！他的感受一定是什么？他本来满心欢喜地期待着这次会面，却奇怪地变成了痛苦。但我并不是他悲伤的见证人，因为我已经毫无生气，很长很长一段时间都没有恢复知觉。

This was the commencement of a nervous fever which confined me for several months. During all that time Henry was my only nurse. I afterwards learned that, knowing my father’s advanced age and unfitness for so long a journey, and how wretched my sickness would make Elizabeth, he spared them this grief by concealing the extent of my disorder. He knew that I could not have a more kind and attentive nurse than himself; and, firm in the hope he felt of my recovery, he did not doubt that, instead of doing harm, he performed the kindest action that he could towards them.
这是神经性发烧的开始，这种发烧使我禁锢了几个月。在那段时间里，亨利是我唯一的护士。后来我才知道，他知道我父亲年事已高，身体不适合长途旅行，也知道我的病会让伊丽莎白变得多么悲惨，所以他隐瞒了我病情的严重程度，从而免除了他们的痛苦。他知道我找不到比他更友善、更细心的护士了。他坚定地希望我能康复，他毫不怀疑，他没有对他们造成伤害，而是尽其所能地对他们做了最仁慈的事情。

But I was in reality very ill, and surely nothing but the unbounded and unremitting attentions of my friend could have restored me to life. The form of the monster on whom I had bestowed existence was forever before my eyes, and I raved incessantly concerning him. Doubtless my words surprised Henry; he at first believed them to be the wanderings of my disturbed imagination, but the pertinacity with which I continually recurred to the same subject persuaded him that my disorder indeed owed its origin to some uncommon and terrible event.
但实际上我病得很重，当然，只有我朋友无限和不懈的关注才能让我复活。我赋予其存在的怪物的形体永远在我眼前，我不停地对他赞叹不已。毫无疑问，我的话让亨利感到惊讶。起初他相信这些是我混乱的想象力的漫游，但我不断地重复同一主题的执着使他相信我的混乱确实归因于一些不寻常和可怕的事件。

By very slow degrees, and with frequent relapses that alarmed and grieved my friend, I recovered. I remember the first time I became capable of observing outward objects with any kind of pleasure, I perceived that the fallen leaves had disappeared and that the young buds were shooting forth from the trees that shaded my window. It was a divine spring, and the season contributed greatly to my convalescence. I felt also sentiments of joy and affection revive in my bosom; my gloom disappeared, and in a short time I became as cheerful as before I was attacked by the fatal passion.
我慢慢地康复了，而且病情频繁复发，这让我的朋友感到震惊和悲伤。我记得当我第一次能够以任何形式的乐趣观察外部物体时，我发现落叶已经消失，新芽正在从遮住窗户的树上抽出。那是一个神圣的春天，这个季节对我的康复有很大帮助。我也感到喜悦和感情在我的怀里复苏。我的忧郁消失了，不久我就变得像被致命的激情袭击之前一样开朗。

‘Dearest Clerval,’ exclaimed I, ‘how kind, how very good you are to me. This whole winter, instead of being spent in study, as you promised yourself, has been consumed in my sick room. How shall I ever repay you? I feel the greatest remorse for the disappointment of which I have been the occasion, but you will forgive me.’
“最亲爱的克莱瓦尔，”我惊呼道，“你对我真好，真好。”这整个冬天，并没有像你向自己承诺的那样，花在学习上，而是在我的病房里度过。我该如何报答你呢？我对自己所造成的失望感到非常悔恨，但你会原谅我的。”

‘You will repay me entirely if you do not discompose yourself, but get well as fast as you can; and since you appear in such good spirits, I may speak to you on one subject, may I not?’
“如果你不心烦意乱，而是尽快康复，你就会完全报答我；既然你看起来精神这么好，我可以和你谈谈一个话题，可以吗？

I trembled. One subject! What could it be? Could he allude to an object on whom I dared not even think?
我颤抖着。一题！会是什么呢？他会不会提到一个我根本不敢想的物体？

‘Compose yourself,’ said Clerval, who observed my change of colour, ‘I will not mention it if it agitates you; but your father and cousin would be very happy if they received a letter from you in your own handwriting. They hardly know how ill you have been and are uneasy at your long silence.’
“冷静一下，”克莱瓦尔观察到我脸色的变化，说道，“如果这件事让你感到不安，我就不会提及；因为这件事会让你感到不安。”但如果你的父亲和表弟收到你亲笔写的信，他们会很高兴。他们几乎不知道你病得有多严重，并且对你长时间的沉默感到不安。

‘Is that all, my dear Henry? How could you suppose that my first thought would not fly towards those dear, dear friends whom I love and who are so deserving of my love?’
“就这些了吗，我亲爱的亨利？你怎么能认为我的第一个念头不会飞向那些我爱的、值得我爱的亲爱的朋友呢？

‘If this is your present temper, my friend, you will perhaps be glad to see a letter that has been lying here some days for you; it is from your cousin, I believe.’
“如果这就是你现在的脾气，我的朋友，你也许会很高兴看到这几天放在这里给你的一封信；我相信是你表弟寄来的。”

Chapter 6
第6章

Clerval then put the following letter into my hands. It was from my own Elizabeth:
然后克莱瓦尔将下面的信交给了我。这是我自己的伊丽莎白写的：

My dearest Cousin,
我最亲爱的表弟，

You have been ill, very ill, and even the constant letters of dear kind Henry are not sufficient to reassure me on your account. You are forbidden to write—to hold a pen; yet one word from you, dear Victor, is necessary to calm our apprehensions. For a long time I have thought that each post would bring this line, and my persuasions have restrained my uncle from undertaking a journey to Ingolstadt. I have prevented his encountering the inconveniences and perhaps dangers of so long a journey, yet how often have I regretted not being able to perform it myself! I figure to myself that the task of attending on your sickbed has devolved on some mercenary old nurse, who could never guess your wishes nor minister to them with the care and affection of your poor cousin. Yet that is over now: Clerval writes that indeed you are getting better. I eagerly hope that you will confirm this intelligence soon in your own handwriting.
你病了，病得很重，即使是亲爱的亨利不断地写信也不足以让我对你放心。你被禁止写字——拿笔；然而，亲爱的维克多，你的一句话对于平息我们的忧虑是必要的。很长一段时间以来，我一直以为每个帖子都会带来这句话，我的劝说阻止了我叔叔前往因戈尔施塔特。我阻止了他遭遇长途旅行的不便甚至危险，但我多少次为自己无法亲自完成而感到遗憾！我心想，照顾你病床的任务已经转移到了某个唯利是图的老护士身上，她永远猜不到你的愿望，也无法像你可怜的表弟一样关心和爱护你。但现在一切都结束了：克莱瓦尔写道，你确实正在变得更好。我热切地希望您能尽快亲笔确认这一情报。

Get well—and return to us. You will find a happy, cheerful home and friends who love you dearly. Your father’s health is vigorous, and he asks but to see you, but to be assured that you are well; and not a care will ever cloud his benevolent countenance. How pleased you would be to remark the improvement of our Ernest! He is now sixteen and full of activity and spirit. He is desirous to be a true Swiss and to enter into foreign service, but we cannot part with him, at least until his elder brother return to us. My uncle is not pleased with the idea of a military career in a distant country, but Ernest never had your powers of application. He looks upon study as an odious fetter; his time is spent in the open air, climbing the hills or rowing on the lake. I fear that he will become an idler unless we yield the point and permit him to enter on the profession which he has selected.
康复并回到我们身边。你会找到一个幸福、快乐的家和深爱你的朋友。你父亲的健康状况很好，他只想见你一面，但他确信你一切都很好。任何忧虑都不会遮掩他仁慈的面容。如果您评价我们欧内斯特的进步，您会感到多么高兴！他现在十六岁了，精力充沛，精神抖擞。他渴望成为一个真正的瑞士人并进入外交部门，但我们不能与他分开，至少在他的哥哥回到我们身边之前是这样。我叔叔对在遥远的国家从事军事生涯的想法不满意，但欧内斯特从来没有像你这样申请的权力。他把学习视为可憎的枷锁；他的时间都花在户外，爬山或在湖上划船。我担心他会成为一个闲人，除非我们让步并允许他从事他所选择的职业。

Little alteration, except the growth of our dear children, has taken place since you left us. The blue lake and snow-clad mountains—they never change; and I think our placid home and our contented hearts are regulated by the same immutable laws. My trifling occupations take up my time and amuse me, and I am rewarded for any exertions by seeing none but happy, kind faces around me. Since you left us, but one change has taken place in our little household. Do you remember on what occasion Justine Moritz entered our family? Probably you do not; I will relate her history, therefore, in a few words. Madame Moritz, her mother, was a widow with four children, of whom Justine was the third. This girl had always been the favourite of her father, but through a strange perversity, her mother could not endure her, and after the death of M. Moritz, treated her very ill. My aunt observed this, and when Justine was twelve years of age, prevailed on her mother to allow her to live at our house. The republican institutions of our country have produced simpler and happier manners than those which prevail in the great monarchies that surround it. Hence there is less distinction between the several classes of its inhabitants; and the lower orders, being neither so poor nor so despised, their manners are more refined and moral. A servant in Geneva does not mean the same thing as a servant in France and England. Justine, thus received in our family, learned the duties of a servant, a condition which, in our fortunate country, does not include the idea of ignorance and a sacrifice of the dignity of a human being.
自从您离开我们以来，除了我们亲爱的孩子们的成长之外，几乎没有发生什么变化。蓝色的湖水，雪山，从未改变；我认为我们平静的家和我们满足的心都受到同样不可改变的法则的调节。我的琐事占用了我的时间并让我开心，而我的任何努力都会得到回报，因为我看到周围只有快乐、友善的面孔。自从你离开我们之后，我们这个小家却发生了一些变化。你还记得贾斯汀·莫里茨什么时候进入我们家吗？也许你不知道；因此，我将用几句话讲述她的历史。她的母亲莫里茨夫人是一位寡妇，有四个孩子，贾斯汀排行老三。这个女孩一直是她父亲的最爱，但由于一种奇怪的反常，她的母亲无法忍受她，莫里茨先生去世后，对她非常不好。我姨妈注意到了这一点，当贾斯汀十二岁的时候，她说服了她的母亲让她住在我们家。我国的共和制度比周围的伟大君主国所盛行的制度更简单、更快乐。因此，其居民的不同阶级之间的区别较小。而下层阶级，既不那么贫穷，也不那么受人轻视，他们的举止更加优雅和道德。日内瓦的仆人与法国和英国的仆人的含义不同。贾斯汀因此被接纳在我们的家庭中，学会了仆人的职责，在我们幸运的国家，这一条件不包括无知和牺牲人类尊严的观念。

Justine, you may remember, was a great favourite of yours; and I recollect you once remarked that if you were in an ill humour, one glance from Justine could dissipate it, for the same reason that Ariosto gives concerning the beauty of Angelica—she looked so frank-hearted and happy. My aunt conceived a great attachment for her, by which she was induced to give her an education superior to that which she had at first intended. This benefit was fully repaid; Justine was the most grateful little creature in the world: I do not mean that she made any professions; I never heard one pass her lips, but you could see by her eyes that she almost adored her protectress. Although her disposition was gay and in many respects inconsiderate, yet she paid the greatest attention to every gesture of my aunt. She thought her the model of all excellence and endeavoured to imitate her phraseology and manners, so that even now she often reminds me of her.
你可能还记得，贾斯汀是你最喜欢的人。我记得你曾经说过，如果你心情不好，贾斯汀的一个眼神就能驱散它，就像阿里奥斯托对安吉丽卡的美丽的评价一样——她看起来如此坦诚和快乐。我姨妈对她产生了很大的依恋，因此她被诱使给她提供比她最初想要的更好的教育。该福利已全部偿还；贾斯汀是世界上最懂得感恩的小生灵：我并不是说她从事任何职业；她只是一个人。我从来没有听到过她的嘴唇，但你可以从她的眼睛里看出她几乎崇拜她的保护者。虽然她性格开朗，在很多方面都不顾及别人的感受，但她却对姨妈的一举一动都格外留意。她认为她是一切优秀的典范，并努力模仿她的措辞和举止，所以即使现在她也经常让我想起她。

When my dearest aunt died every one was too much occupied in their own grief to notice poor Justine, who had attended her during her illness with the most anxious affection. Poor Justine was very ill; but other trials were reserved for her.
当我最亲爱的姨妈去世时，每个人都沉浸在自己的悲伤中，没有注意到可怜的贾斯汀，她在她生病期间以最焦虑的感情照顾着她。可怜的贾斯汀病得很重。但还有其他的考验是留给她的。

One by one, her brothers and sister died; and her mother, with the exception of her neglected daughter, was left childless. The conscience of the woman was troubled; she began to think that the deaths of her favourites was a judgment from heaven to chastise her partiality. She was a Roman Catholic; and I believe her confessor confirmed the idea which she had conceived. Accordingly, a few months after your departure for Ingolstadt, Justine was called home by her repentant mother. Poor girl! She wept when she quitted our house; she was much altered since the death of my aunt; grief had given softness and a winning mildness to her manners which had before been remarkable for vivacity. Nor was her residence at her mother’s house of a nature to restore her gaiety. The poor woman was very vacillating in her repentance. She sometimes begged Justine to forgive her unkindness but much oftener accused her of having caused the deaths of her brothers and sister. Perpetual fretting at length threw Madame Moritz into a decline, which at first increased her irritability, but she is now at peace for ever. She died on the first approach of cold weather, at the beginning of this last winter. Justine has returned to us, and I assure you I love her tenderly. She is very clever and gentle and extremely pretty; as I mentioned before, her mien and her expressions continually remind me of my dear aunt.
她的兄弟姐妹一一死去；她的母亲除了被忽视的女儿外，没有孩子。女人的良心不安；她开始认为，她最爱的人的死是上天对她偏心的惩罚。她是一名罗马天主教徒；我相信她的忏悔神父证实了她的想法。因此，在您前往因戈尔施塔特几个月后，贾斯汀被她悔改的母亲叫回家。可怜的姑娘！当她离开我们家时，她哭了；自从我姨妈去世后，她发生了很大的变化。悲伤给她的举止带来了温柔和迷人的温和，而这在以前是非常活泼的。她住在母亲家里也无法恢复她的快乐。这个可怜的女人在悔改方面非常犹豫不决。她有时恳求贾斯汀原谅她的不友善，但更常见的是指责她造成了她兄弟姐妹的死亡。持续不断的烦躁最终使莫里茨夫人陷入了衰弱，这使她起初更加烦躁，但现在她永远平静了。去年冬天初，她在寒冷天气第一次来临的时候去世了。贾斯汀回到了我们身边，我向你保证我温柔地爱着她。她非常聪明、温柔，而且非常漂亮；正如我之前提到的，她的举止和表情不断让我想起我亲爱的阿姨。

I must say also a few words to you, my dear cousin, of little darling William. I wish you could see him; he is very tall of his age, with sweet laughing blue eyes, dark eyelashes, and curling hair. When he smiles, two little dimples appear on each cheek, which are rosy with health. He has already had one or two little *wives*, but Louisa Biron is his favourite, a pretty little girl of five years of age.
我还必须对你说几句话，我亲爱的表弟，关于小宝贝威廉。我希望你能见到他；他的个子在同龄人中很高，有一双甜甜的、笑起来的蓝眼睛、深色的睫毛和卷曲的头发。当他微笑时，双颊上都会出现两个小酒窝，红润健康。他已经有一两个小“妻子”了，但路易莎·拜伦是他的最爱，一个五岁的漂亮小女孩。

Now, dear Victor, I dare say you wish to be indulged in a little gossip concerning the good people of Geneva. The pretty Miss Mansfield has already received the congratulatory visits on her approaching marriage with a young Englishman, John Melbourne, Esq. Her ugly sister, Manon, married M. Duvillard, the rich banker, last autumn. Your favourite schoolfellow, Louis Manoir, has suffered several misfortunes since the departure of Clerval from Geneva. But he has already recovered his spirits, and is reported to be on the point of marrying a very lively, pretty Frenchwoman, Madame Tavernier. She is a widow, and much older than Manoir, but she is very much admired and a favourite with everybody.
现在，亲爱的维克多，我敢说您希望沉迷于有关日内瓦善良人民的一些八卦。美丽的曼斯菲尔德小姐已经因与年轻的英国人约翰·墨尔本先生即将结婚而受到了祝贺。去年秋天，她丑陋的妹妹曼农 (Manon) 嫁给了富有的银行家杜维拉德先生 (M. Duvillard)。自从克莱瓦尔离开日内瓦以来，你最喜欢的同学路易斯·马努瓦遭受了几次不幸。但他已经恢复了精神，据报道即将与一位非常活泼、漂亮的法国女人塔维尼尔夫人结婚。她是一位寡妇，比马诺尔年长很多，但她深受大家的钦佩和喜爱。

I have written myself into better spirits, dear cousin; but my anxiety returns upon me as I conclude. Write, dearest Victor—one line—one word will be a blessing to us. Ten thousand thanks to Henry for his kindness, his affection, and his many letters; we are sincerely grateful. Adieu! My cousin, take care of yourself, and, I entreat you, write!
我已经把自己写得精神好多了，亲爱的表弟；但当我得出结论时，我的焦虑又回来了。写吧，最亲爱的维克多——一行——一个字将成为我们的祝福。万分感谢亨利的好意、他的感情以及他的许多来信；我们衷心感谢。再见！我的表弟，照顾好自己，我恳求你，写信！

Elizabeth Lavenza
伊丽莎白·拉文扎

Geneva, March 18th, 17—
2017 年 3 月 18 日，日内瓦——

‘Dear, dear Elizabeth!’ I exclaimed when I had read her letter. ‘I will write instantly and relieve them from the anxiety they must feel.’ I wrote, and this exertion greatly fatigued me; but my convalescence had commenced, and proceeded regularly. In another fortnight I was able to leave my chamber.
“亲爱的，亲爱的伊丽莎白！”读完她的信后，我惊呼道。 “我会立即写信，让他们摆脱他们必须感受到的焦虑。”我写道，这种努力让我感到非常疲倦。但我的康复已经开始，并且有规律地进行。又过了两周，我就可以离开我的房间了。

One of my first duties on my recovery was to introduce Clerval to the several professors of the university. In doing this, I underwent a kind of rough usage, ill befitting the wounds that my mind had sustained. Ever since the fatal night, the end of my labours, and the beginning of my misfortunes, I had conceived a violent antipathy even to the name of natural philosophy. When I was otherwise quite restored to health, the sight of a chemical instrument would renew all the agony of my nervous symptoms. Henry saw this, and had removed all my apparatus from my view. He had also changed my apartment, for he perceived that I had acquired a dislike for the room which had previously been my laboratory. But these cares of Clerval were made of no avail when I visited the professors. M. Waldman inflicted torture when he praised, with kindness and warmth, the astonishing progress I had made in the sciences. He soon perceived that I disliked the subject, but not guessing the real cause, he attributed my feelings to modesty and changed the subject from my improvement to the science itself, with a desire, as I evidently saw, of drawing me out. What could I do? He meant to please, and he tormented me. I felt as if he had placed carefully, one by one, in my view those instruments which were to be afterwards used in putting me to a slow and cruel death. I writhed under his words yet dared not exhibit the pain I felt. Clerval, whose eyes and feelings were always quick in discerning the sensations of others, declined the subject, alleging, in excuse, his total ignorance; and the conversation took a more general turn. I thanked my friend from my heart, but I did not speak. I saw plainly that he was surprised, but he never attempted to draw my secret from me; and although I loved him with a mixture of affection and reverence that knew no bounds, yet I could never persuade myself to confide to him that event which was so often present to my recollection but which I feared the detail to another would only impress more deeply.
康复后我的首要任务之一就是向大学的几位教授介绍克莱瓦尔。在这样做的过程中，我经历了一种粗暴的使用，与我心灵所受的创伤不相符。自从那个致命的夜晚，我的劳动结束，我的不幸开始以来，我什至对自然哲学的名字都产生了强烈的反感。当我的健康完全恢复时，一看到化学仪器就会让我的神经症状再次感到痛苦。亨利看到了这一点，并把我所有的仪器从我的视野中移开。他还换了我的公寓，因为他发现我已经不喜欢这个以前是我实验室的房间了。但当我拜访教授们时，克莱瓦尔的这些关心并没有起到什么作用。沃尔德曼先生善意而热情地赞扬我在科学上取得的惊人进步，这对我来说是一种折磨。他很快就意识到我不喜欢这个主题，但没有猜测真正的原因，他将我的感觉归因于谦虚，并将主题从我的进步转向科学本身，正如我显然看到的那样，他希望把我拉出来。我能做什么？他本意是为了取悦我，但他却在折磨我。我觉得他好像在我看来，小心翼翼地把那些工具一一放置在我的眼前，这些工具后来将被用来缓慢而残酷地处死我。他的话让我浑身翻腾，却又不敢表现出我的痛苦。克莱瓦尔的眼睛和感觉总是能够迅速辨别他人的感受，他拒绝了这个话题，借口说自己完全无知。谈话转向了更广泛的话题。我发自内心地感谢我的朋友，但我没有说话。 我清楚地看出他很惊讶，但他从未试图从我嘴里套出我的秘密。虽然我对他怀着无限的爱意和崇敬之情，但我永远无法说服自己向他吐露那件事，这件事经常出现在我的记忆中，但我担心细节给别人只会留下更深刻的印象。 。

M. Krempe was not equally docile; and in my condition at that time, of almost insupportable sensitiveness, his harsh, blunt encomiums gave me even more pain than the benevolent approbation of M. Waldman. ‘D—n the fellow!’ cried he. ‘Why, M. Clerval, I assure you he has outstripped us all. Ay, stare if you please; but it is nevertheless true. A youngster who, but a few years ago, believed in Cornelius Agrippa as firmly as in the Gospel, has now set himself at the head of the university; and if he is not soon pulled down, we shall all be out of countenance. Ay, ay,’ continued he, observing my face expressive of suffering, ‘M. Frankenstein is modest, an excellent quality in a young man. Young men should be diffident of themselves, you know, M. Clerval; I was myself when young; but that wears out in a very short time.’
克伦佩先生并不同样温顺。在我当时的情况下，几乎无法忍受的敏感，他严厉、直率的赞美给我带来的痛苦比沃尔德曼先生的仁慈的赞许还要多。 “该死的家伙！”他喊道。 “哎呀，克莱瓦尔先生，我向你保证他已经超越了我们所有人。哎呀，如果你愿意的话，就盯着看吧；但这确实是事实。几年前，这位年轻人还像福音书一样坚定地相信哥尼流·阿格里帕，如今却成为了大学的校长；如果不尽快把他打倒，我们都会面无表情。哎呀，哎呀，”他继续说道，观察着我脸上流露出痛苦的表情，“M。弗兰肯斯坦为人谦虚，这是年轻人身上的优秀品质。克莱瓦尔先生，你知道，年轻人应该对自己感到自信。年轻时我还是我自己；但它会在很短的时间内磨损。”

M. Krempe had now commenced a eulogy on himself, which happily turned the conversation from a subject that was so annoying to me.
克伦佩先生现在开始为自己写悼词，这很高兴地把话题从令我讨厌的话题上转移了。

Clerval had never sympathized in my tastes for natural science, and his literary pursuits differed wholly from those which had occupied me. He came to the university with the design of making himself complete master of the Oriental languages, as thus he should open a field for the plan of life he had marked out for himself. Resolved to pursue no inglorious career, he turned his eyes towards the East as affording scope for his spirit of enterprise. The Persian, Arabic, and Sanskrit languages engaged his attention, and I was easily induced to enter on the same studies. Idleness had ever been irksome to me, and now that I wished to fly from reflection and hated my former studies, I felt great relief in being the fellow pupil with my friend, and found not only instruction but consolation in the works of the Orientalists. I did not, like him, attempt a critical knowledge of their dialects, for I did not contemplate making any other use of them than temporary amusement. I read merely to understand their meaning, and they well repaid my labours. Their melancholy is soothing, and their joy elevating, to a degree I never experienced in studying the authors of any other country. When you read their writings, life appears to consist in a warm sun and a garden of roses, in the smiles and frowns of a fair enemy, and the fire that consumes your own heart. How different from the manly and heroical poetry of Greece and Rome!
克莱瓦尔从来不认同我对自然科学的兴趣，他的文学追求也与我所追求的完全不同。他来到大学，是为了让自己完全掌握东方语言，为自己制定的人生计划开辟一片天地。他决心不再追求不光彩的职业，将目光投向了东方，因为东方为他的进取精神提供了发挥的空间。波斯语、阿拉伯语和梵语吸引了他的注意力，我很容易就被吸引进入同样的研究。懒惰一直让我感到厌烦，现在我想逃避反思，讨厌以前的学习，与我的朋友成为同学让我感到极大的解脱，在东方学家的著作中不仅得到了指导，而且得到了安慰。我没有像他一样尝试对他们的方言进行批判性的了解，因为除了暂时的娱乐之外，我没有考虑将它们用于任何其他用途。我阅读只是为了理解它们的含义，它们很好地回报了我的劳动。他们的忧郁令人舒缓，他们的欢乐令人振奋，达到了我在研究任何其他国家的作家时从未体验过的程度。当你阅读他们的作品时，你会发现生活似乎包含在温暖的阳光和玫瑰花园中，存在于公平敌人的微笑和皱眉中，以及吞噬你自己内心的火焰中。与希腊、罗马的男子气概和英雄主义诗歌多么不同啊！

Summer passed away in these occupations, and my return to Geneva was fixed for the latter end of autumn; but being delayed by several accidents, winter and snow arrived, the roads were deemed impassable, and my journey was retarded until the ensuing spring. I felt this delay very bitterly, for I longed to see my native town and my beloved friends. My return had only been delayed so long from an unwillingness to leave Clerval in a strange place before he had become acquainted with any of its inhabitants. The winter, however, was spent cheerfully, and although the spring was uncommonly late, when it came its beauty compensated for its dilatoriness.
夏天就这样过去了，我回到日内瓦的时间定在秋末。但由于几次事故的耽误，冬天和雪到来，道路无法通行，我的行程被推迟到来年春天。我对这种耽搁感到非常痛苦，因为我渴望见到我的家乡和我亲爱的朋友。我的归程只被推迟了这么长时间，因为我不愿意在克莱瓦尔熟悉那里的任何居民之前将他留在一个陌生的地方。然而，冬天却是愉快地度过的，虽然春天来得异常晚，但它的美丽弥补了它的迟缓。

The month of May had already commenced, and I expected the letter daily which was to fix the date of my departure, when Henry proposed a pedestrian tour in the environs of Ingolstadt, that I might bid a personal farewell to the country I had so long inhabited. I acceded with pleasure to this proposition: I was fond of exercise, and Clerval had always been my favourite companion in the rambles of this nature that I had taken among the scenes of my native country.
五月已经开始，我每天都期待着这封信，确定我的出发日期，当时亨利提议步行游览英戈尔施塔特的郊区，这样我就可以向我长久以来的国家告别了。居住过。我高兴地接受了这个提议：我喜欢锻炼，克莱瓦尔一直是我在祖国的风景中漫步时最喜欢的同伴。

We passed a fortnight in these perambulations; my health and spirits had long been restored, and they gained additional strength from the salubrious air I breathed, the natural incidents of our progress, and the conversation of my friend. Study had before secluded me from the intercourse of my fellow creatures and rendered me unsocial, but Clerval called forth the better feelings of my heart; he again taught me to love the aspect of nature and the cheerful faces of children. Excellent friend! How sincerely did you love me and endeavour to elevate my mind until it was on a level with your own! A selfish pursuit had cramped and narrowed me until your gentleness and affection warmed and opened my senses; I became the same happy creature who, a few years ago, loved and beloved by all, had no sorrow or care. When happy, inanimate nature had the power of bestowing on me the most delightful sensations. A serene sky and verdant fields filled me with ecstasy. The present season was indeed divine; the flowers of spring bloomed in the hedges, while those of summer were already in bud. I was undisturbed by thoughts which during the preceding year had pressed upon me, notwithstanding my endeavours to throw them off, with an invincible burden.
我们在这些巡视中度过了两个星期。我的健康和精神早已恢复，并且从我呼吸的有益健康的空气、我们前进的自然事件以及我朋友的谈话中获得了额外的力量。以前，学习使我无法与同胞交流，使我变得不合群，但克莱瓦尔唤起了我内心更好的感觉；他再次教会我热爱大自然的一面和孩子们快乐的面孔。优秀的朋友！你是多么真诚地爱我，并努力提升我的思想，直到它与你的思想处于同一水平！自私的追求让我变得狭窄和狭窄，直到你的温柔和深情温暖并打开了我的感官；我又变成了几年前那个被所有人爱着、被爱着、没有悲伤、没有忧虑的快乐生物。当快乐时，无生命的大自然有能力赋予我最令人愉悦的感觉。宁静的天空和翠绿的田野让我心旷神怡。现在的季节确实是神圣的。春天的花朵在树篱中绽放，而夏天的花朵已经含苞待放。我并没有被前一年压在我身上的想法所困扰，尽管我以不可战胜的负担努力摆脱它们。

Henry rejoiced in my gaiety and sincerely sympathized in my feelings; he exerted himself to amuse me, while he expressed the sensations that filled his soul. The resources of his mind on this occasion were truly astonishing; his conversation was full of imagination, and very often, in imitation of the Persian and Arabic writers, he invented tales of wonderful fancy and passion. At other times he repeated my favourite poems or drew me out into arguments, which he supported with great ingenuity.
亨利为我的快乐感到高兴，并真诚地同情我的感受。他一边竭尽全力地逗我开心，一边表达着他灵魂深处的感受。这次他的脑力真是惊人。他的谈话充满想象力，而且常常模仿波斯和阿拉伯作家，编造出充满奇思妙想和激情的故事。其他时候，他会重复我最喜欢的诗歌，或者让我陷入争论，他以极大的独创性支持我的观点。

We returned to our college on a Sunday afternoon; the peasants were dancing, and everyone we met appeared gay and happy. My own spirits were high, and I bounded along with feelings of unbridled joy and hilarity.
周日下午我们回到了大学。农民们在跳舞，我们遇到的每个人都显得快乐而快乐。我自己的情绪很高涨，我带着无拘无束的喜悦和欢闹的感觉跳跃着。

Chapter 7
第7章

On my return, I found the following letter from my father:—
回来后，我发现了父亲写的以下信：——

‘My dear Victor,
“我亲爱的维克多，

‘You have probably waited impatiently for a letter to fix the date of your return to us; and I was at first tempted to write only a few lines, merely mentioning the day on which I should expect you. But that would be a cruel kindness, and I dare not do it. What would be your surprise, my son, when you expected a happy and glad welcome, to behold, on the contrary, tears and wretchedness? And how, Victor, can I relate our misfortune? Absence cannot have rendered you callous to our joys and griefs; and how shall I inflict pain on my long absent son? I wish to prepare you for the woeful news, but I know it is impossible; even now your eye skims over the page to seek the words which are to convey to you the horrible tidings.
“你可能已经不耐烦地等待一封信来确定你返回我们的日期；起初我只想写几行，只是提到我应该等你的那一天。但这是一种残忍的善意，我不敢这么做。我的儿子，当你期待着幸福和高兴的欢迎时，看到的却是泪水和悲伤，你会感到惊讶吗？维克多，我该如何讲述我们的不幸呢？缺席不会让你对我们的欢乐和悲伤麻木不仁；我该如何让我久违的儿子痛苦呢？我想让你对这个不幸的消息做好准备，但我知道这是不可能的；即使是现在，你的眼睛仍在页面上浏览，寻找那些向你传达可怕消息的文字。

William is dead!—that sweet child, whose smiles delighted and warmed my heart, who was so gentle, yet so gay! Victor, he is murdered! I will not attempt to console you; but will simply relate the circumstances of the transaction.
威廉死了！——那个可爱的孩子，他的笑容让我高兴，温暖了我的心，他是那么温柔，却又那么快乐！维克多，他被谋杀了！我不会试图安慰你；但只会简单地叙述交易的情况。

Last Thursday (May 7th), I, my niece, and your two brothers, went to walk in Plainpalais. The evening was warm and serene, and we prolonged our walk farther than usual. It was already dusk before we thought of returning; and then we discovered that William and Ernest, who had gone on before, were not to be found. We accordingly rested on a seat until they should return. Presently Ernest came, and enquired if we had seen his brother; he said, that he had been playing with him, that William had run away to hide himself, and that he vainly sought for him, and afterwards waited for a long time, but that he did not return.
上周四（5月7日），我、我的侄女和你的两个兄弟去Plainpalais散步。夜晚温暖而宁静，我们比平常走得更远。等我们想回去的时候，已经是黄昏了。然后我们发现先前出发的威廉和欧内斯特不见了。因此，我们在座位上休息，直到他们回来。不久，欧内斯特来了，询问我们是否见过他的兄弟。他说，他一直在和他玩耍，威廉逃跑躲藏起来，他徒劳地寻找他，后来等了很长时间，但他没有回来。

This account rather alarmed us, and we continued to search for him until night fell, when Elizabeth conjectured that he might have returned to the house. He was not there. We returned again, with torches; for I could not rest, when I thought that my sweet boy had lost himself, and was exposed to all the damps and dews of night; Elizabeth also suffered extreme anguish. About five in the morning I discovered my lovely boy, whom the night before I had seen blooming and active in health, stretched on the grass livid and motionless; the print of the murderer’s finger was on his neck.
这个说法让我们相当震惊，我们继续寻找他，直到夜幕降临，这时伊丽莎白推测他可能已经回到了房子。他不在那儿。我们带着火把又回来了；因为当我想到我可爱的孩子已经迷失了自己，并暴露在夜晚的所有潮湿和露水中时，我无法休息。伊丽莎白也遭受了极大的痛苦。早上五点左右，我发现了我可爱的孩子，前一天晚上我还看到他健康活泼地绽放着，现在他脸色铁青，一动不动地躺在草地上。凶手的手指印在他的脖子上。

He was conveyed home, and the anguish that was visible in my countenance betrayed the secret to Elizabeth. She was very earnest to see the corpse. At first I attempted to prevent her; but she persisted, and entering the room where it lay, hastily examined the neck of the victim, and clasping her hands exclaimed, ‘O God! I have murdered my darling child!’
他被送回家，我脸上明显的痛苦向伊丽莎白泄露了这个秘密。她很迫切地想看到尸体。起初我试图阻止她，但她没有这么做。但她坚持不懈，走进了尸体所在的房间，匆忙检查了受害者的脖子，并紧握双手惊呼：“上帝啊！我谋杀了我亲爱的孩子！

She fainted, and was restored with extreme difficulty. When she again lived, it was only to weep and sigh. She told me, that that same evening William had teased her to let him wear a very valuable miniature that she possessed of your mother. This picture is gone, and was doubtless the temptation which urged the murdered to the deed. We have no trace of him at present, although our exertions to discover him are unremitted; but they will not restore my beloved William!
她晕了过去，好不容易才恢复过来。当她再活过来的时候，只剩下哭泣和叹息。她告诉我，那天晚上威廉取笑她让他戴上她拥有的你母亲的一个非常珍贵的微型模型。这张照片已经消失了，无疑是促使被谋杀者采取行动的诱惑。尽管我们一直在努力寻找他，但目前我们还没有找到他的踪迹。但他们不会挽回我心爱的威廉！

Come, dearest Victor; you alone can console Elizabeth. She weeps continually, and accuses herself unjustly as the cause of his death; her words pierce my heart. We are all unhappy; but will not that be an additional motive for you, my son, to return and be our comforter? Your dear mother! Alas, Victor! I now say, Thank God she did not live to witness the cruel, miserable death of her youngest darling!
来吧，最亲爱的维克多；只有你才能安慰伊丽莎白。她不停地哭泣，并不公正地指责自己是造成他死亡的原因。她的话刺痛了我的心。我们都不快乐；但这难道不会成为你，我的儿子，回来安慰我们的额外动机吗？你亲爱的妈妈！唉，维克多！我现在要说，感谢上帝，她没有活着亲眼目睹她最小的宝贝残酷而悲惨的死亡！

Come, Victor; not brooding thoughts of vengeance against the assassin, but with feelings of peace and gentleness, that will heal, instead of festering, the wounds of our minds. Enter the house of mourning, my friend, but with kindness and affection for those who love you, and not with hatred for your enemies.
来吧，维克多；不是沉思着向刺客报仇，而是带着平静和温柔的感觉，这会治愈我们心灵的伤口，而不是使其溃烂。进入哀悼之家，我的朋友，但要带着对爱你的人的仁慈和感情，而不是对你的敌人的仇恨。

Your affectionate and afflicted father,
你深情而痛苦的父亲，

Alphonse Frankenstein.
阿尔方斯·弗兰肯斯坦。

Geneva, May 12th, 17—.
2017 年 5 月 12 日，日内瓦——。

Clerval, who had watched my countenance as I read this letter, was surprised to observe the despair that succeeded the joy I at first expressed on receiving new from my friends. I threw the letter on the table, and covered my face with my hands.
当我读这封信时，克莱瓦尔一直注视着我的表情，他惊讶地发现，我在收到朋友的来信时最初表现出的喜悦之后，又出现了绝望。我把信扔在桌子上，用手捂住脸。

‘My dear Frankenstein,’ exclaimed Henry, when he perceived me weep with bitterness, ‘are you always to be unhappy? My dear friend, what has happened?’
“我亲爱的弗兰肯斯坦，”亨利看到我痛苦地哭泣，大声说道，“你总是不快乐吗？我亲爱的朋友，发生了什么事？

I motioned him to take up the letter, while I walked up and down the room in the extremest agitation. Tears also gushed from the eyes of Clerval, as he read the account of my misfortune.
我示意他拿起这封信，而我则极其激动地在房间里走来走去。当克莱瓦尔读到我的不幸经历时，他的眼里也涌出了泪水。

‘I can offer you no consolation, my friend,’ said he; ‘your disaster is irreparable. What do you intend to do?’
“我无法给你任何安慰，我的朋友，”他说。 ‘你的灾难是无法挽回的。你打算做什么？

‘To go instantly to Geneva: come with me, Henry, to order the horses.’
“立即前往日内瓦：跟我来，亨利，去订购马匹。”

During our walk, Clerval endeavoured to say a few words of consolation; he could only express his heartfelt sympathy. ‘Poor William!’ said he, dear lovely child, he now sleeps with his angel mother! Who that had seen him bright and joyous in his young beauty, but must weep over his untimely loss! To die so miserably; to feel the murderer’s grasp! How much more a murderer that could destroy radiant innocence! Poor little fellow! one only consolation have we; his friends mourn and weep, but he is at rest. The pang is over, his sufferings are at an end for ever. A sod covers his gentle form, and he knows no pain. He can no longer be a subject for pity; we must reserve that for his miserable survivors.’
在我们散步的过程中，克莱瓦尔尽力说了几句安慰的话。他只能表示衷心的同情。 “可怜的威廉！”他说，亲爱的可爱的孩子，他现在和他天使般的母亲一起睡觉！谁见过他年轻时的美丽容光焕发，却必须为他的过早逝去而哭泣！死得这么惨；感受凶手的掌握！何况是一个能够摧毁光辉纯真的凶手！可怜的小家伙！我们唯一的安慰就是；他的朋友们哀悼哭泣，但他却安息了。痛苦结束了，他的痛苦永远结束了。草皮覆盖着他温柔的身躯，他感觉不到疼痛。他不能再成为怜悯的对象；我们必须为他悲惨的幸存者保留它。

Clerval spoke thus as we hurried through the streets; the words impressed themselves on my mind and I remembered them afterwards in solitude. But now, as soon as the horses arrived, I hurried into a cabriolet, and bade farewell to my friend.
当我们匆匆穿过街道时，克莱瓦尔这样说道。这句话深深地印在我的脑海里，后来我在孤独中想起了它们。但现在，马一到，我就赶紧钻进一辆敞篷车，向我的朋友告别。

My journey was very melancholy. At first I wished to hurry on, for I longed to console and sympathise with my loved and sorrowing friends; but when I drew near my native town, I slackened my progress. I could hardly sustain the multitude of feelings that crowded into my mind. I passed through scenes familiar to my youth, but which I had not seen for nearly six years. How altered every thing might be during that time! One sudden and desolating change had taken place; but a thousand little circumstances might have by degrees worked other alterations, which, although they were done more tranquilly, might not be the less decisive. Fear overcame me; I dared no advance, dreading a thousand nameless evils that made me tremble, although I was unable to define them.
我的旅程非常忧郁。起初我想快点走，因为我渴望安慰和同情我所爱的和悲伤的朋友；但当我接近我的家乡时，我放慢了脚步。我几乎无法承受涌入我脑海的多种感觉。我看到了我年轻时熟悉的场景，但我已经有近六年没有见过了。在那段时间里，一切都发生了多么大的变化！一场突如其来、令人悲凉的变化发生了。但是，一千个小情况可能会逐渐产生其他变化，尽管这些变化进行得更加平静，但可能不会那么具有决定性。恐惧战胜了我；我不敢前进，害怕着一千种无名的邪恶，让我颤抖，尽管我无法定义它们。

I remained two days at Lausanne, in this painful state of mind. I contemplated the lake: the waters were placid; all around was calm; and the snowy mountains, ‘the palaces of nature,’ were not changed. By degrees the calm and heavenly scene restored me, and I continued my journey towards Geneva.
我在洛桑呆了两天，心情十分痛苦。我凝视着湖面：湖水平静；周围一片平静；而雪山，“自然的宫殿”，却没有改变。平静而神圣的景象逐渐让我恢复了平静，我继续前往日内瓦。

The road ran by the side of the lake, which became narrower as I approached my native town. I discovered more distinctly the black sides of Jura, and the bright summit of Mont Blanc. I wept like a child. ‘Dear mountains! my own beautiful lake! how do you welcome your wanderer? Your summits are clear; the sky and lake are blue and placid. Is this to prognosticate peace, or to mock at my unhappiness?’
路沿着湖边延伸，越接近我的家乡，路就越窄。我更清楚地发现了侏罗山的黑色侧面和勃朗峰的明亮顶峰。我哭得像个孩子。 ‘亲爱的山啊！我自己美丽的湖！你如何欢迎你的流浪者？你的顶峰是清晰的；天空和湖水蔚蓝而平静。这是在预示和平，还是在嘲笑我的不幸？

I fear, my friend, that I shall render myself tedious by dwelling on these preliminary circumstances; but they were days of comparative happiness, and I think of them with pleasure. My country, my beloved country! who but a native can tell the delight I took in again beholding thy streams, thy mountains, and, more than all, thy lovely lake!
我的朋友，我担心我会因纠缠于这些初步情况而使自己变得乏味。但那是相对幸福的日子，我很高兴地想起它们。我的祖国，我亲爱的祖国！只有本地人才能说出我再次看到你的溪流、你的山脉，尤其是你美丽的湖泊时所感受到的喜悦！

Yet, as I drew nearer home, grief and fear again overcame me. Night also closed around; and when I could hardly see the dark mountains, I felt still more gloomily. The picture appeared a vast and dim scene of evil, and I foresaw obscurely that I was destined to become the most wretched of human beings. Alas! I prophesied truly, and failed only in one single circumstance, that in all the misery I imagined and dreaded, I did not conceive the hundredth part of the anguish I was destined to endure.
然而，当我临近家时，悲伤和恐惧再次笼罩了我。夜幕也降临了；当我几乎看不到黑暗的山脉时，我的心情更加黯淡。画面中出现了一片浩瀚而昏暗的邪恶景象，我隐隐约约地预见到，我注定会成为人类中最悲惨的人。唉!我的预言是真实的，只有一种情况是失败的：在我想象和害怕的所有痛苦中，我没有想象到我注定要忍受的痛苦的百分之一。

It was completely dark when I arrived in the environs of Geneva; the gates of the town were already shut; and I was obliged to pass the night at Secheron, a village at the distance of half a league from the city. The sky was serene; and, as I was unable to rest, I resolved to visit the spot where my poor William had been murdered. As I could not pass through the town, I was obliged to cross the lake in a boat to arrive at Plainpalais. During this short voyage I saw the lightning playing on the summit of Mont Blanc in the most beautiful figures. The storm appeared to approach rapidly, and, on landing, I ascended a low hill, that I might observe its progress. It advanced; the heavens were clouded, and I soon felt the rain coming slowly in large drops, but its violence quickly increased.
当我到达日内瓦郊区时，天已经完全黑了。城门已经关闭。我不得不在距离城市半里格的一个村庄塞什隆过夜。天空很平静；由于无法休息，我决定去看看我可怜的威廉被谋杀的地方。由于无法穿过城镇，我不得不乘船过湖到达平原宫。在这次短暂的航行中，我看到了闪电在勃朗峰顶上以最美丽的身影玩耍。风暴似乎正在迅速逼近，着陆后，我爬上了一座低矮的山丘，以便观察它的进展。它进步了；天空乌云密布，我很快就感觉到雨点慢慢地落下，但雨势很快就加大了。

I quitted my seat, and walked on, although the darkness and storm increased every minute, and the thunder burst with a terrific crash over my head. It was echoed from Saleve, the Juras, and the Alps of Savoy; vivid flashes of lightning dazzled my eyes, illuminating the lake, making it appear like a vast sheet of fire; then for an instant every thing seemed of a pitchy darkness, until the eye recovered itself from the preceding flash. The storm, as is often the case in Switzerland, appeared at once in various parts of the heavens. The most violent storm hung exactly north of the town, over the part of the lake which lies between the promontory of Belrive and the village of Copet. Another storm enlightened Jura with faint flashes; and another darkened and sometimes disclosed the Mole, a peaked mountain to the east of the lake.
我离开座位，继续前行，尽管黑暗和暴风雨每分钟都在加剧，雷声在我头顶上发出可怕的撞击声。萨莱维、侏罗山和萨沃伊阿尔卑斯山也有类似的声音。鲜明的闪电使我眼花缭乱，照亮了湖面，使它看起来像一片巨大的火。有一瞬间，一切都变得一片漆黑，直到眼睛从先前的闪光中恢复过来。这场风暴就像瑞士经常发生的那样，同时出现在天空的各个地方。最猛烈的风暴袭击了该镇的正北地区，位于贝尔里夫海角和科佩特村之间的湖区。另一场风暴照亮了汝拉地区，发出微弱的闪光。另一幅图使鼹鼠山变暗，有时甚至露出来，这是湖东边的一座尖峰山。

While I watched the tempest, so beautiful yet terrific, I wandered on with a hasty step. This noble war in the sky elevated my spirits; I clasped my hands, and exclaimed aloud, ‘William, dear angel! this is thy funeral, this thy dirge!’ As I said these words, I perceived in the gloom a figure which stole from behind a clump of trees near me; I stood fixed, gazing intently: I could not be mistaken. A flash of lightning illuminated the object, and discovered its shape plainly to me; its gigantic stature, and the deformity of its aspect, more hideous than belongs to humanity, instantly informed me that it was the wretch, the filthy daemon, to whom I had given life. What did he there? Could he be (I shuddered at the conception) the murderer of my brother? No sooner did that idea cross my imagination, than I became convinced of its truth; my teeth chattered, and I was forced to lean against a tree for support. The figure passed me quickly, and I lost it in the gloom. Nothing in human shape could have destroyed the fair child. He was the murderer! I could not doubt it. The mere presence of the idea was an irresistible proof of the fact. I thought of pursuing the devil; but it would have been in vain, for another flash discovered him to me hanging among the rocks of the nearly perpendicular ascent of Mont Saleve, a hill that bounds Plainpalais on the south. He soon reached the summit, and disappeared.
我一边看着美丽又可怕的暴风雨，一边快步走着。这场崇高的天空之战振奋了我的精神；我紧握双手，大声喊道：“威廉，亲爱的天使！”这是你的葬礼，这是你的挽歌！’当我说这些话时，我在黑暗中看到一个人影从我附近的一丛树后面偷偷地走来；我定定地站着，凝视着：我不会弄错的。一道闪电照亮了那个物体，我清楚地发现了它的形状。它巨大的身躯和畸形的外表，比人类更可怕，立即告诉我，它是我赋予生命的可怜虫，肮脏的恶魔。他在那里做什么？他会不会是（一想到这个我就不寒而栗）谋杀我兄弟的凶手？这个想法一出现在我的想象中，我就确信它是真实的。我的牙齿打颤，我被迫靠在一棵树上支撑。那个身影很快就从我身边掠过，我在黑暗中迷失了方向。任何人形都无法摧毁这个美丽的孩子。他就是凶手！我无法怀疑这一点。这个想法的存在本身就是不可抗拒的事实证明。我想到去追赶魔鬼；但这是徒劳的，因为我再次一闪，发现他挂在萨莱维山几乎垂直的山坡上的岩石中，山上是普兰帕莱南边的一座山。很快他就到达了山顶，然后就消失了。
